Current Commentary

Borrowing and Bond Issues Proceed Simultaneously 23

— A Cold Observer

Since the autumn of last year, financial conditions have tightened sharply, and all industries have declined. The cities have followed the countryside and presented a desolate scene. In order to rescue the financial situation, the authorities are negotiating with the United Kingdom, the United States, and other countries for a loan of 10 million pounds, while simultaneously issuing financial bonds worth 100 million yuan to expand bank capital. This dual approach aims to achieve the practical effect of circulating the economy and supporting industry and commerce. The bond regulations have now been passed by the Legislative Yuan, and the loan of 10 million pounds will be issued within days. Although the loan is still under negotiation, it is not certain whether it will succeed. However, according to foreign newspapers, international cooperation to rescue our country's finances seems to be a possibility. If the loan can be successfully secured, what impact will it have on our country's economy?

When the order to increase the silver export tax was first promulgated, those who did not understand the truth made reckless speculations, believing that inflation might be inevitable. As a result, capital fled, and silver continued to flow out. Later, the authorities repeatedly stated that they would not do this, and the news of the loan being pursued simultaneously spread in domestic and foreign newspapers. As a result, doubts were dispelled, and people's minds gradually settled down. The loan plan is the opposite of the inflation policy. If the goal is inflation, there is no need to rely on a loan. The decision to pursue a loan is clear evidence that inflation will not be adopted. This is why people's minds have suddenly become more stable. With people's minds at ease, capital will no longer flee, and the outflow of silver can be temporarily suppressed.

Our country's foreign trade has always been in deficit. Previously, we were fortunate to have large remittances from overseas Chinese and inflows of foreign capital to offset the deficit. In recent years, remittances have decreased sharply, and there has been less investment. International income has been insufficient to cover expenses, and gold and silver have been continuously exported, which is difficult to reverse. Although the economic recession has reduced purchasing power, foreign goods are not selling as well as in previous years. However, the decline in exports remains sluggish, and the imbalance persists. The amount of gold stored domestically is not large, and silver is needed to fill reserves, so how can we allow it to continue to flow out? Since it is difficult to export gold and silver to offset the deficit, we must rely on overseas credit. In order to stop the outflow of silver, the authorities are making every effort to secure a loan, which does not seem to be an inappropriate strategy to rescue the tight financial situation.

If the loan can be secured, it will ease the financial situation and provide some relief to the government's finances. It is a quick fix, and this measure is not entirely unreasonable. If we can address both the symptoms and the root causes, by using the proceeds of the loan to purchase construction materials and focusing on developing farmland and revitalizing water conservancy, domestic agricultural production will increase significantly, and food imports will decrease. At the same time, we should try to control unnecessary consumption to prevent the import of luxury goods, and implement the abolition of transit taxes and the reduction of export taxes to encourage the export of domestic goods. The trend of trade deficits may be reversed. If we can maintain the gold and silver stored domestically, the risk of financial tightening can be avoided.

Anglo-Russian Talks Continue, Touching on Far East Problems; Maintaining China's Territorial Integrity and Economic Trade are Also Under Consideration 49

(Moscow) When Eden and Litvinov continued their talks today, the Far East issue was the main event for discussion. Although details could not be obtained from official sources, it is widely believed that maintaining peace in the Far East and China's integrity are both under consideration. It is reported that several economic issues, loans to Russia, and the impact of the Ottawa Agreement on Anglo-Russian trade, especially timber, were also mentioned. This morning's talks lasted for one and a half hours and were conducted in the same sincere and trusting spirit as yesterday.

Eden and Stalin Have a Heart-to-Heart Talk

After lunch at the British Embassy, Eden went to Stalin's private room at 4:00 PM for a sincere conversation. Molotov, the Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars, was also present. The meeting took place in a simply furnished long room with only portraits of Marx and Engels hanging on the walls. Through the windows, one could see the high walls of the Administrative Yuan. At the same time, attention is currently being paid here to the reorganization of the Polish government, and there is much speculation as to whether the new government will favor Germany to some extent. As Eden will be going to Warsaw in a few days, everyone is particularly concerned. There was heavy snow here yesterday, but this morning when Eden went from the embassy to meet with Litvinov, the sun was shining brightly, a completely different climate from yesterday. (29th Reuters Dispatch)

Japan Declares Policy Unchanged

(Tokyo) As rumors spread that the Anglo-Russian talks, which have attracted worldwide attention, will discuss the Far East issue, the Japanese Foreign Ministry stated that although the Anglo-Russian talks will discuss the Far East issue, Japan's established Far East policy will never be changed, expressing the following views: The European situation is very different from before World War I, and its influence on the Far East is not as significant as before. We do not need to be concerned about the recent ever-changing European situation. Although the contents of the Anglo-German talks in Berlin cannot be known for sure, it seems to be a fact that Germany advocates strengthening its armaments against Russia. The worsening of German-Russian relations is a problem that can be noted in the future. The strengthening of German armaments has forced Soviet Russia to strengthen its defenses on the western European border, thereby reducing its defense efforts in the Far East. Therefore, it may not be known that it wants to obtain some kind of guarantee on this point. However, Japan has a definite policy on the Far East issue, implements its policy according to its own views, and will never be affected by the European situation. (29th Japanese United Press Dispatch)

(Tokyo) A Foreign Ministry spokesman stated today that no matter what changes occur in the overall European situation, Japan's policies towards foreign countries such as Soviet Russia will not be affected. Japan's foreign policy, as stated by the Foreign Minister in the Diet, is non-aggressive and non-threatening, and aims to maintain peace in the Far East. Japan has no plans to invade neighboring countries, but is prepared to rise up and defend them when peace is endangered. Asahi Shimbun carried an editorial stating that the only way out for the great powers is to give Germany some satisfaction and induce it to join a new peace pact. It also mentioned overseas comments speculating that Japan will take advantage of the newly arising disputes in the European situation and act freely in the Far East, saying that Japan has no intention of "fishing in troubled waters." (29th Reuters Dispatch)

This afternoon, Eden and Litvinov talked for two hours. The result seems to have made the United Kingdom and Russia more understanding of each other. Grand Banquet in Moscow: Anglo-Russian Exchange of Speeches, War Crisis Looms Over Europe, Talks Between the Two Countries are the Starting Point for Cooperation 52

(Moscow) Tonight, Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov hosted a banquet to welcome British representative Eden. The grandeur was unprecedented in Moscow for many years. Litvinov gave a speech on the spot, and after it was over, he raised a glass to wish the British Emperor a long life. Since the establishment of the Soviet regime, this is the first time that a state official has raised a glass to wish the Emperor a long life. (28th Reuters Dispatch)

(Moscow) Litvinov hosted a banquet yesterday to welcome Eden. Those accompanying him were Defense Commissar Voroshilov, Railways Commissar Kaganovich, Heavy Industry Commissar Ordzhonikidze, Deputy Chairman of the People's Committee Mezhlauk, Finance Commissar Grinko, Food Industry Commissar Mikoyan, Foreign Trade Commissar Rozengolts, Posts and Telecommunications Commissar Rykov, and other members of the Soviet government, British Ambassador Chilston and his wife, Lord Cranborne, Soviet Ambassador to the United Kingdom Maisky (who came to the Soviet Union with Eden), Strong, head of the League of Nations group of the Foreign Affairs Committee, staff of the British Embassy, and senior officials of the Foreign Affairs Committee.

Welcome Speech by Russian Foreign Minister

Litvinov gave a welcome speech on the spot, saying, "Mr. Eden's visit is an important milestone in the history of Soviet-British relations. Economic and cultural relations between the two countries have their normal and satisfactory development, and progress has also been obvious in the political aspect. Our country has long known what the people of your country are understanding. For example, Mr. Chamberlain recently said that the development of Soviet-British friendly relations is not hindered by anyone, and Mr. Zhang also said that "this kind of relationship is extremely important in preserving peace." At present, the work of preserving the normal international order has encountered serious and surprising difficulties. At this time, Mr. Ai's visit is extremely important, so its significance is especially important. Since the World War, there has never been such a great worry about the fate of peace as it is today. This kind of worry is the common feeling of all friends of peace and the vast masses of all countries. If they are not anesthetized by militarism and patriotism, they will surely be friends of peace for a long time. The largest number of countries at present yearn to preserve peace. There may be some exceptions at this time, but these dangerous places must at least be confined to one corner and clearly defined. Although, being able to confine them to one corner does not mean that they have been confined to one corner. We have no such intelligence to accurately predict that one country or certain countries will be greatly harmed by them, because this kind of danger is advancing in all directions. This situation has led all countries to urgently seek ways to hinder this kind of danger. Today, it is unanimously believed that if we want to completely eliminate the war crisis in Europe and the world, or reduce the degree of risk to the lowest limit, we can only rely on the cooperative efforts of all countries, especially the great powers.

When British policy signed an agreement with France on February 3, it took a step forward towards jointly preserving peace. It is precisely for this reason that the Soviet government welcomes the London Agreement with great enthusiasm and is determined to fully cooperate. The Soviet Union and the United Kingdom are located at the extreme east of Europe and the extreme west of Europe, and both are adjacent to other continents. Therefore, I believe that Anglo-Soviet cooperation is of decisive importance for peace, and your visit is not only the beginning of this cooperation, but also a guarantee for its long-term continuation. European politicians must be able to discern that the destruction of peace in any part of Europe will have extremely bad consequences. At the same time, they are aware that they bear a great responsibility. In the coming months or weeks, we will see whether they can organize peace in the way that the current international situation urgently requires, and implement the cooperation plan set on February 3 to obtain its wise and logical conclusion. However, in any case, Mr. Eden's frank exchange of views with me and my colleagues will surely contribute greatly to this work," he said.

Mr. Eden's Response

Then Eden gave a reply, first thanking Litvinov for his kind welcome, and said that he was very pleased with what Litvinov said about this visit opening a new stage in the development of Anglo-Soviet relations. Although this trip is purely exploratory in nature and has no negotiating significance, "However, we can say that this first cordial conversation is indeed a remarkable and hopeful (I believe it is) milestone in the relations between our two countries," said Eden. Eden recalled the League of Nations' invitation to the Soviet Union to join the alliance, and stated that the British government's foreign policy is based on the League of Nations, and reiterated the importance of the Soviet Union's accession to the League of Nations. Eden also said that peace and improving diplomatic relations are the main purposes of the League of Nations, and at the same time, peace is the primary goal of British foreign policy. "I believe that this point must be the concern of the Soviet Union and other countries where the main purpose of all countries is to seek the well-being of their people. I firmly believe that this situation can only be improved by the representatives of the world's major powers talking frankly and exchanging views. This belief has not weakened since I recently visited various places. The main point of this trip is also here. The purpose of the subsequent Stresa foreign ministers' meeting and our meeting today is to find a way to get out of the current European predicament. These paths must be honest and respectable for all countries, and at the same time, be in line with the principle of cooperative security that we firmly believe in. Although we have differences in other issues, the above is our common position. I would also like to deeply believe that we will be able to move forward firmly to maintain peace," he said. After the meeting, there was a grand reception, attended by representatives of the diplomatic corps, Soviet public institutions, and domestic and foreign journalists. (29th TASS Dispatch)

Security Issues: Wide Discrepancies in Anglo-German Views; Opposition Between "National" and "Group" Theories; Simon Reports to the House of Commons 53

(London) According to Reuters' diplomatic correspondent, although the detailed facts of the Anglo-German talks are still being kept secret, it is gradually becoming clear that the "large differences of opinion" that Foreign Minister Simon stated in the House of Commons refer to fundamental principles. The visit to Berlin by Simon and Eden has not brought the different attitudes of the United Kingdom and Germany on the issue of group security closer. The current situation seems to be crystallizing into a political opposition between the "national" theory and the "group" theory. The British authorities now have to decide what attitude they should take towards European issues in the future. Eden's visits to Moscow, Warsaw, and Prague will be of vital importance to this point. What can now be assumed is that Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov will use the results of the Anglo-German discussions in Berlin as new argumentative material for supporting the Eastern European Convention. (29th Reuters Dispatch)

(London) Foreign Minister Simon reported on the progress of the Anglo-German talks in the House of Commons today, tacitly admitting that there was no progress in the Anglo-German negotiations. Simon admitted that German leader Hitler's attitude was strong, so that the result of the talks had "discovered large differences of opinion." However, the Foreign Minister did not express despair, and said that the result of the talks had been quite valuable, and that both sides were able to understand each other's views. Simon also solemnly declared that this trip was only the first British consultation with various European countries, and that the final meeting would be held by representatives of the United Kingdom, France, and Italy in Stresa, so it was not yet possible to explain the general situation in detail. As for the scope of the Berlin talks, it included all European issues and Germany's relationship to these issues. The Associated Press also learned from semi-official sources that Hitler had requested at least the return of one territory and the formal abolition of the military clauses of the Treaty of Versailles as conditions for Germany's return to the League of Nations. (28th National Telegram)

What Will Britain Do?

(Paris) After British Foreign Minister Simon made a statement in the House of Commons yesterday, admitting that the views of the United Kingdom and Germany were far apart, the newspapers here commented that Hitler's five demands, revealed by the London Daily Telegraph, were actually true, even though the German government denied them. This can be evidenced by the speech of Foreign Minister Simon. "Le Petit Parisien" said, "The content of the denial issued by Germany only involves two of the five demands, namely (1) the return of the Polish Corridor to Germany, and (2) the return of the German minority settlement in the Czech Republic to Germany. This kind of denial is neither complete nor was it published until yesterday, so it is difficult for world opinion to trust it. As such, there is no doubt about the breadth of the demands made by Germany. Foreign Minister Simon did not hesitate to say that the opinions of the United Kingdom and Germany differed, but in order to observe diplomatic etiquette, he deliberately used vague words, but the negative impression that occurred on the first day of the Anglo-German talks has indeed proven to be true," "Paris Echo" reported, "It is easy for Germany to issue a denial, but if its content is clearer, and more detailed about what Hitler said and what he refrained from saying, then the world will be easier to believe," "Business Report" reported, "The United Kingdom now has two attitudes that it can take. One is to let Germany do whatever it wants, and the other is to actively organize a security system to deal with German hegemony. Foreign Minister Simon has already made it clear about all of this," and so on. (29th Havas Dispatch)

Attitude of Various Factions in Parliament

(London) Foreign Minister Simon frankly stated in the House of Commons today that the views of the United Kingdom and Germany are very different, which impressed people in parliament, because the conditions put forward by Germany, which were published in several newspapers recently, were generally true. The people in parliament have already known it very well. According to these newspapers, the conditions for Germany's return to the League of Nations are so shocking that the Conservative Party believes that these conditions are absolutely unacceptable. Therefore, they only hope that the countries in the Stresa meeting will maintain close contact to jointly ensure collective security. In the future, if Germany changes its demands, it will be allowed to join various collective security conventions. The Conservative Party especially supports the conclusion of a mutual assistance treaty in Western Europe, because if something happens in Western Europe, the United Kingdom will inevitably be drawn into the vortex due to its geographical location. In addition, other mutual assistance conventions can be supported by the British government through purely diplomatic means, without direct participation. The opinions of the Conservative Party are generally like this. As for the Liberal Party and the Labour Party, they are quite disappointed by the too broad demands put forward by Germany, because the opposition parties of the Liberal Party and the Labour Party originally wanted to blame the responsibility for the failure of the talks on the government, so as to question the government. Now that Germany's requirements are so harsh, they turn to making the opposition parties unable to criticize the government. Some Labour MPs said that Hitler's demands are the maximum demands, and they will surely be greatly reduced after negotiations with France. In short, the attitude of the Liberal Party and the Labour Party will largely be determined when Simon presents a report after the Stresa meeting. If Simon's report shows that Germany's tough attitude is irreversible, then the position of the Liberal Party and the Labour Party will naturally be weakened, because there is nothing to attack the government with. (28th Havas Agency Dispatch)

Germany's Demands: Recovering Pre-War Lost Territories, Including Japanese-Administered Islands, as a Condition for Anglo-German Alliance 54

(London) The Daily Telegraph reports that the German government, during talks in Berlin, proposed the recovery of pre-war colonies as a condition for rejoining the League of Nations and establishing an Anglo-German alliance, thereby obtaining what Kaiser Wilhelm II called "a place in the sun." The Anglo-German alliance plan would correspond with all of Germany's demands, and the colonies lost after the war should be returned to their original owners. Regarding this, Hitler mentioned Japan, saying that the country is no longer a member of the League of Nations, so how can it retain the Pacific mandated islands? The Daily Mail reports that Hitler, during the talks, confirmed to Simon that the German air force is now superior in number to the British air force. (29th, Havas dispatch)

Peace or War: The Old Generation Knows the Choice 55

(Moscow) News from London indicates that the British Cabinet is about to propose that after the Anglo-French-Italian conference in Stresa, an international conference of European countries be convened. Those around Lord Privy Seal Eden believe this should be treated with reservation. A close associate of Eden recently told this agency's reporter, "Everything will depend on the information we receive. Our trip is to consult various opinions and gather suggestions to provide research material for the British government, so that we may know whether a general agreement is possible within a defined scope. The British generally advocate the establishment of a security pact and have no intention of rejecting Germany. However, if Germany continues to reject it herself, or if she removes the essence of the pact while retaining its shell, it will be impossible to avoid responsibility. This is because one must choose between establishing security with effective laws or departing from the path of security and waiting for war to break out." (29th, Havas dispatch)

Hitler Inspects the Air Force 56

(Berlin) German leader Hitler, in his capacity as Supreme Commander of the National Defense Forces, today inspected the Dobritz air force together with Generals Göring and Milch. During the inspection, General Göring first reported on the situation of the force, and Hitler then personally inspected it. The aircraft performed various skills in the air, and Hitler praised them highly, calling them an elite force established after the founding of the German Air Force. (29th, National Telegram)

German Labor Front Leader Explains the Purpose of Labor Service: Assisting Compulsory Military Service and Eliminating Class Struggle 57

(Berlin) The leader of the German Labor Service, Mr. Hierl, gave a speech in Leipzig today, foreshadowing the imminent implementation of compulsory labor service to assist compulsory military service. Mr. Hierl said that unified compulsory labor service can create a new type of worker, consolidate the conscript army, eliminate class differences, promote national affairs, and ensure an abundant food supply. (28th, Reuters dispatch)

Leipzig: The German Workers' Vanguard recently held a conference here. Mr. Hierl, the leader of the German Labor Front, made an important declaration at the conference today, stating that Germany's reintroduction of conscription and the needs and purposes of national labor service are in no way contradictory or restrictive. Mr. Hierl further stated that foreign misinterpretations of German national labor service as a substitute for military service are a distortion, because military service and labor service are completely different and cannot be substituted for each other. The duty of the national defense force is to defend the borders from attack, while labor service is the practical application of national socialism, guaranteeing that national sentiment will no longer be divided by class struggle. Mr. Hierl solemnly declared at the end, "In the future, national labor service should be implemented before military service. Anyone who wishes to earn the honor of a soldier must first prove their national value with honorable service in the labor corps. This principle is especially important for the leaders of the national defense force, regardless of their rank, and they must receive national socialist training in the labor corps. Therefore, in the future, German citizens, after receiving dual training in labor service and military service, will become new citizens completely immersed in national socialism, and the future of the country will rest on their shoulders. Therefore, the premise of the nation's future and the supreme law are all embodied in the words 'serving the country.'" (28th, National Telegram)

Rumors of Ribbentrop's Dismissal Due to Information Leaks 58

(Berlin) When British cabinet members visited Germany recently, Hitler's confidant Ribbentrop participated in the talks. Last night, rumors circulated that Ribbentrop had been dismissed because the Anglo-German talks failed to maintain strict secrecy, and much of the information was leaked in the newspapers. Ribbentrop should be held responsible. (29th, Havas dispatch)

French Foreign Minister Decides on Date to Visit Russia: Departure Set for the 10th of Next Month, Russian Foreign Minister Sends Telegram of Welcome 59

I believe that exchanging opinions at this time will be more effective than our previous talks. At the same time, this move will complete a new stage in establishing closer relations and cooperation between our two countries, as well as finding effective guarantees for peace." Laval replied in his telegram, "I am deeply grateful for your warm regards. I wish to inform you that as soon as the international conferences to be held on April 10th and 15th allow me the opportunity, I will accept the invitation of the Soviet government with deep pleasure. I believe that our talks in Moscow in the near future will complete a new victory in the friendship and cooperation between France and the Soviet Union, for the development of universal security and the consolidation of peace." The Little Entente Closely United with France: Meeting Between Romanian and French Foreign Ministers 61

It is reported that Titulescu stayed briefly in the capitals of Yugoslavia and Czechoslovakia, and his visit represents the Little Entente expressing close unity with France, and especially a willingness to firmly adhere to and not allow any shaking of various treaties and the League of Nations Covenant. In addition, France and the Little Entente countries have always believed in the collective security system proposed in the London Declaration. (29th, Havas dispatch)

German Naval Demands: The United States Remains Indifferent, Shipbuilding Program Intensifies 63

(Washington) According to responsible sources, the United States is almost completely indifferent to Germany's demand for a navy of 400,000 tons. Since the failure of the Anglo-Japanese-American London Naval Talks at the end of last year, Britain has proposed to hold new talks on a broader basis in the hope of establishing an international agreement to replace the Washington Naval Treaty, and has advocated that secondary naval powers such as Germany participate in the talks. At that time, the U.S. government had already expressed that it had no objections, because the U.S. considers maintaining the 5:5:3 ratio to be the most important issue, and is not very concerned about whether or not secondary European countries expand their navies. (28th, Havas dispatch)

(Washington) As the European situation becomes increasingly tense, the leaders of the House of Representatives are today rapidly carrying out large-scale national defense actions. Westinghouse Electric Corporation in New York announced that it has received a naval order to undertake the electrical equipment for 18 new destroyers, worth 1.75 million dollars. The Navy Department is actively spending the shipbuilding funds from Congress, which is evident from this. At a time when Congress is accelerating the passage of national defense plans, peace organizations across the country are unanimously opposed to the militarization of the United States. The Anti-War Association of England held a meeting in Worcester, Massachusetts, and passed a motion requesting President Roosevelt not to hold this summer's naval exercises near the Sea of Japan. US Pacific Aviation: Ideal Gradually Becoming Reality, "Oriental Clipper" Departs from Mexico, Wake and Other Island Stations to Be Completed Within Six Months 64

San Diego: The ideal of Pacific aviation is gradually becoming a reality. The giant aircraft "Oriental Clipper" landed here today. The mail ship "North Haven" also departed from San Francisco this morning with 118 people to Wake Island and Midway Island to open up the airfield and necessary housing, which will take at least six months. Of the 188 people, 44 are experts. (28th, National Telegram)

Austrian Royal Family Restoration: Receiving Italian and French Support, According to Hungarian Newspaper 66

Warsaw: Relations between Poland and Germany have been quite tense recently. (28th, Havas dispatch)

The three cabinet members resigned to protest, and as a result, the government had no choice but to resign en masse. (19th, Reuters dispatch)

Belgian Premier Announces: Abandoning the Gold Standard, Recognizing Soviet Russia, and Devaluing Currency by Up to 30%; Bank Notes Will Also Cease Gold Redemption 72

Brussels – The Belgian Parliament convened today to hear the new cabinet announce its major policies. The chamber was packed, and the audience listened intently, displaying unprecedented tension. The new Prime Minister, Théophile de Jongh, declared that the government had decided to temporarily abandon the gold standard and had also decided to recognize Soviet Russia. The devaluation of the Belgian franc would officially take effect on Sunday, March 31, with a maximum devaluation of 30%. As for the recognition of the Soviet Russian government, no date was announced, but given the instability in Europe, Belgium's formal resumption of relations with Soviet Russia would be implemented as soon as possible. Various parties were quite satisfied with Prime Minister de Jongh's declaration. Supporters of the government's policies in Parliament accounted for a majority of 40 to 50. The Prime Minister indicated informally that the purchase of 2,000,000,000 francs' worth of gold in the past two months, coupled with large withdrawals of gold from banks, had contributed to the financial panic. The Prime Minister also announced that the redemption of Belgian banknotes for gold would also be temporarily suspended. After an international financial agreement is established in the future, efforts would be made to restore the gold standard. He also stated that Belgium would strive to facilitate this international agreement. (National Telegram, 29th)

Brussels – Belgium has decided to devalue the Belgian franc. The government formed by former Vice Governor of the National Bank of Belgium, Théophile de Jongh, announced today that Belgium would still adhere to the gold standard but would reduce the value of its currency. The extent of the reduction would be limited to 30%. The gold reserves of the National Bank of Belgium would be temporarily revalued based on a standard that reduces the currency value by 25% compared to its current value. This morning, the Belgian cabinet read a proclamation to the Chamber of Representatives regarding this matter, stating that the government acknowledged that it was impossible to protect the Belgian franc at the previously set standard. Therefore, the exchange rate of the Belgian franc must be revised. The obligation of the National Bank to pay on demand, as stipulated in the 1926 regulations, would be temporarily suspended. It was also stated that the Belgian cabinet intends to use its full strength to promote an international mechanism that can restabilize the world's major currencies in terms of gold. (Reuters, 29th)

Brussels – After the new Prime Minister, Théophile de Jongh, took office, it was heard that he had formulated the cabinet's administrative guidelines and would soon submit them to Parliament. The outline is divided into nine items as follows:

(1) Devalue the Belgian currency by 25% to maintain a comparable exchange rate with the British pound.

(2) Establish an exchange stabilization fund.

(3) Launch public works projects to relieve unemployment and promote trade.

(4) The National Bank will control other banks; all enterprises must first prove their foundation is solid before they can be granted loans by the National Bank.

(5) Appropriately reduce certain tariffs to lower prices.

(6) Establish a 40-hour work week.

(7) Convene an international conference to stabilize the currencies of various countries.

(8) Restore diplomatic relations with Russia.

(9) The Chamber of Representatives will adjourn for one year. (Havas, 28th)

(London) The Belgian government's order for the stock exchange to close for three days is seen here as a precursor to the country's devaluation of its currency. As a result, the Belgian currency has begun to depreciate in foreign markets. The Belgian currency against the British exchange rate fell today from 271.75 Belgian francs (equivalent to one pound) to 24 francs, before recovering to 23 francs at the close. (Havas Telegram, 28th)

Brussels – The government has ordered all stock exchanges to close and reopen on Monday. The country is filled with financial panic today, and people generally believe that the value of currency is about to decline, and Belgium will completely abandon the gold standard. The degree of currency devaluation will probably be between 28% and 33%. Those who own physical assets are doing everything possible to protect themselves today, frantically buying property such as houses, jewelry, and clothing, etc. Therefore, the nation's shops are extremely crowded all day long. Leaders of several political parties held small group meetings today and decided that they would vote for a vote of confidence if the new government of Prime Minister Théophile de Jongh can clearly explain its monetary policy plans. However, the cabinet's declaration in Parliament tomorrow will likely only briefly outline the main points of the government's plan. It is learned that de Jongh will request the privilege of managing the currency without the approval of the House of Representatives for a certain period. If so, after the currency devaluation, the government will have the freedom to deal with matters during the initial dangerous period. However, according to the Associated Press, the Congress will continue to meet before formally accepting or rejecting the government's plan. As for the rumors that the new government is about to devalue the currency, the general public believed that it was inevitable this morning. At 10:15 AM, the government ordered the closure of stock exchanges across the country. Although official sources cautiously stated that this move was intended to prevent speculation and did not indicate any panic, non-official sources claimed that after the closure, the government could calmly design a plan to deal with unforeseen circumstances. The general public is paying close attention to the opening of Parliament tomorrow to hear the government's announcement of its major policies, because the new Prime Minister de Jongh has always advocated currency management policies. (National Telegram, 28th)

(Paris) After the Belgian currency fell, those who advocate the French franc gold standard have not changed their attitudes, but people in the business community are gradually advocating lowering the currency value. France's tariff barriers can make exchange rate changes ineffective, so even if the Belgian franc depreciates, the French franc may still not be subject to economic repercussions. However, bankers fear that people will be motivated by profit, sell French government bonds, and invest their idle funds in foreign securities. If so, it will withdraw funds from banks and cause currency inflation, because banks do not have sufficient guarantees for their debts to depositors. (Reuters, 28th)

(New York) The closure of the Belgian stock exchange, which is a prelude to the devaluation of the Belgian currency, did not disrupt the New York financial market, because this development in Belgium was not entirely unexpected. However, after the devaluation of the Belgian currency, what impact will other gold currencies face? This is a matter of much speculation. Some believe that if the gold bloc collapses, the path to the rapid stabilization of currencies in all aspects will be opened up as a result, which will benefit the whole world. Some people regard the method of transferring gold from Paris to New York as the final act of the gold currency farce, but whether Paris actually has gold transported to the United States will depend on the latest developments in Belgium. (Reuters, 28th)

(Paris) The British Exchange Control has shipped gold worth 18 million pounds from London to Paris to pay for the forward pounds purchased when the pound exchange rate was 71 francs, because the British authorities did not have enough francs. This shipment of gold has nothing to do with other gold flows. The demand for US dollars in Paris is increasing due to commercial needs and increased tension. Therefore, gold is continuously flowing into New York. The French financial situation now depends on whether the Netherlands and Switzerland can continue to ship out gold to meet the withdrawal of foreign funds. If these two countries reduce or stop the export of gold, the French authorities will have to find ways to curb the outflow of gold. According to general opinion, the recent political developments in Europe may make the French authorities even more reluctant to lose a large amount of gold. It is rumored that Belgian Prime Minister Théophile de Jongh will propose lowering the value of the Belgian currency to make it 26 Belgian francs to one British gold pound, in other words, devaluing the Belgian franc by 28%. It is generally expected that Belgium will issue 4% Belgian government bonds in London in order to replace domestic Belgian government bonds. (Reuters, 28th)

Brussels – The Belgian cabinet announced in Parliament that it would allow the National Bank to temporarily suspend the payment of gold and declared that it would organize a special agency to supervise the credit policy and exchange rates set by the cabinet. This temporary measure will be effective from February 31st. Belgium temporarily leaves the gold standard, but the government still intends to restore the gold standard in the future. (Reuters, 29th)

(London) Today, Belgian Prime Minister Théophile de Jongh requested Parliament to authorize (1) to reduce the value of the Belgian currency, limited to 30%; (2) to temporarily restrict payments before an international agreement on currency policy is reached. The Belgian Prime Minister proposed to first reduce the currency value by 25%. This is the first break in the gold bloc. The devaluation of the Belgian currency will affect certain Belgian exports to the UK. Belgium has always exported large quantities of steel, but since the pound's value fell, the number of these goods imported into the UK has been greatly reduced. Belgium also manufactures large quantities of cement bricks, and in the future, due to the lower price of the Belgian currency, it will compete with the UK within the UK and overseas. (Reuters, 29th)

(London) London was not shocked after hearing the Belgian decision to lower the currency value, but is waiting for news of any reactions from other gold bloc countries. Financial circles here said that the path adopted by the Belgian cabinet is exactly the same as that previously adopted by President Roosevelt. The Belgian Prime Minister Théophile de Jongh followed President Roosevelt's example and requested Congress to allow him to have the power to devalue to the highest degree without being bound by the final reduced number himself. This is to reserve a powerful tool for future negotiations on stabilizing currency prices. Théophile de Jongh has always admired President Roosevelt and is confident that he can follow in Roosevelt's footsteps and use the paper surplus obtained from revaluing gold reserves to fund the equalization fund. Demand for the British pound in Europe has been quite strong recently. Today's actions by Belgium have made the demand for the British pound even stronger, but the London Stock Exchange has not been affected in any way. People in Paris pointed out that this move by Belgium is a blood transfusion from the gold bloc to the British pound bloc and are now watching whether domestic prices in Belgium can remain stable, as the theory promoted by those in France who advocate for currency devaluation suggests. If its price stability is consistent with this theory, it is predicted that the calls for lowering currency value in France will be even higher than they are now. (Reuters, 29th)

(Tokyo) The Belgian Ambassador to Japan, Baron Albert Bassompierre, visited Vice Minister Shigemitsu of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at noon on the 29th, stating that he plans to travel to China soon. League of Nations Drug Control Efforts 75

(Geneva) The Standing Opium Committee of the League of Nations recently announced that Costa Rica and Ecuador in Central America have recently joined the 1925 Geneva Convention on Drug Control. Therefore, the total number of countries that have joined the convention is fifty-two. Furthermore, since the Greek government ratified the Drug Control Convention in 1931, the total number of countries that have ratified the convention is forty-nine. Regarding the quarterly import and export statistics of narcotics, the Standing Opium Committee recently pointed out that more detailed statistical reports must be obtained first. Some countries in Central and South America do not regularly submit statistical reports to the committee, and they should be requested to submit them in the future. As for the various statistical reports on the achievements obtained during the first year (i.e., 1931) of the implementation of the Drug Control Convention sent by the Secretariat of the League of Nations, the committee has already filed them for the record. It is estimated that the committee handled a total of 29 cases of negotiations to prohibit the export of narcotics in certain countries this year, and the committee considered that more than 100 cases of small amounts of narcotics should not be subject to embargo. (Havas Telegram, 28th)

Japanese Warship Welcomes Pu Yi to Tokyo 76

(Dalian) Pu Yi is scheduled to depart for Japan on April 2nd to visit the Japanese imperial family. Officials from the "Manchukuo" and Japanese governments have gathered here for this event. Pu Yi's entourage consists of a total of 83 people, most of whom have already arrived here. A warship carrying Pu Yi and others to Japan also arrived this afternoon. After arriving in Japan, Pu Yi will stay in Tokyo for ten days, and then visit places such as Nishikyo in western Japan. He is scheduled to return to Manchukuo on April 26th. The Dalian Water Police has now been placed on strict alert. From now until the day Pu Yi returns to Manchukuo, all ships entering the port will be strictly inspected, and 66 Chinese and Japanese personnel will be assigned to secretly monitor Chinese and Japanese ships traveling between Dalian, Shanghai, Qingdao, Weihaiwei, Longkou, Yantai, Tianjin, Tanggu, Nagasaki, Moji, Jemulpo, Andong, and the various ports in Taiwan. (Reuters, 29th)

American Silk Factory Closes Due to Impact of Japanese Dumping 77

New Bedford, Massachusetts - The Butler Silk Factory here closed today. Management announced that the reason for the closure was the inability to compete with Japanese goods. The factory employs 850 workers. (National Telegram, 21st)

International Commercial Telegram – Special Business Report from Reuters on March 29 – 78

Gold and Silver

British Gold: London gold prices fell by one shilling and two and a half pence due to the strong French exchange rate against the pound, to one hundred and forty-three shillings and eight pence.

British Silver: London silver prices fell sharply again today. The spot price is 27.875 pence, a decrease of half a penny, and the futures price is 28 pence, a decrease of .4375. China and speculators sold, and then repurchased when the price fell. The closing market situation was uncertain.

British Silver: The Monterey silver market fell by about 50 pounds due to the weakness of the London silver market.

Exchange Rates

US/US: Since the Belgian government decided to devalue the Belgian franc by 25%, the London foreign exchange market was generally strong for the British pound today, and prices also rose sharply. The opening exchange rate between the US dollar and the British pound was $4.81375, which was .875 higher than yesterday's closing price between the US dollar and the British pound. Prices rose sharply in the morning, and the latest price at 2:00 PM was $4.85125, which was .0375 higher than the opening price.

British/French: The opening price rose by 9 pounds and was 73.03 francs, and then continued to rise. At 2:00 PM, the price was 73.65 francs, which was .61 pounds higher than the opening price.

Cotton and Wheat

US Cotton: The New York cotton market opened down about one pound, with continued sales from foreign countries, but some purchases were made by the industry. Trading was scarce, but morale was still stable. The situation in Europe, the strength of the British pound, favorable weather reports, and the revival of industry interest are all conflicting factors. The trend is still uncertain.

British Cotton: Liverpool cotton prices fell slightly today. At 1:00 PM, the May futures price fell by 5 pounds to 6.11.

Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market price at 1:00 PM for the May futures was 5 shillings and 3 pence, a decrease of .375.

US Wheat: The Chicago wheat market was affected by exchange rates, but weather reports had the power to influence the market. The drought in the winter wheat area remains, with no rain expected. The wheat market opened up .125, and then continued to rise slightly.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market opened weak, and the price became stable when it fell. At noon, the transaction price for July and September futures was 5.875 pence, which was .125 lower than yesterday.

New York: The New York rubber market was affected by weak London telegrams at the opening. The price was 25 to 30 pounds lower than yesterday's closing price. The market price fluctuated narrowly.

Securities

New York: Wall Street this morning expects that the securities market will definitely be very sluggish, because the situation in Belgium is uncertain, and the silver amendment to the work relief bill has been voted down, which has reduced hopes for US currency inflation, and until the domestic situation is clarified, the stock market will inevitably lack impetus. Stock prices opened slightly lower this morning, a situation similar to yesterday. The Dow Jones 30 industrial stock average price was 100.53, a decrease of 2 pounds. After the opening, prices fluctuated limitedly and varied, with no definite trend. The various prices are as follows:
