1934 Soviet Union's Foreign Trade (German Correspondence) 79

Since the implementation of the Second Five-Year Plan, the development of industry in the Soviet Union has become a matter of global astonishment. Especially the figures for foreign trade in 1934 fully demonstrate the Soviet Union's continuous advancement and the gradual possibility of becoming a "self-sufficient" nation. Stalin said some time ago that as a result of the Five-Year Plan, the Soviet Union has changed from a timber country to a steel country. This is not an exaggeration, because the Soviet Union is now in a situation where the bitter days are over and the sweet days have begun.

Years ago, when the Five-Year Plan was mentioned, European newspapers described it with a mocking attitude, ridiculing it as "fantasy". But in recent years, this atmosphere has gradually disappeared and turned into close attention. Even the German newspapers in the past two years, due to the fundamental conflict between National Socialism and Communism, rarely published articles on the current situation in the Soviet Union. However, recently they have changed their direction, and articles discussing the Soviet Union have often been seen in newspapers. It can be seen that in recent years, the progress of the Soviet Union has been deeply noticed by both enemies and friends.

From January to October 1934, the total amount of Soviet Union's foreign trade in ten months was 533.6 million rubles. Similarly, in the ten months of 1933, the total amount was 701.5 million rubles. In the ten months of 1932, the total amount even reached 1,058.6 million rubles. According to this figure, from 1932 to 1934, the total foreign trade of the Soviet Union has almost halved in two years. If it were in a capitalist country, it would naturally be the result of being affected by the global economic panic and a sign of decline. However, the Soviet Union is a socialist country. The purpose of foreign trade is to seek more elements for the development of domestic industry, which is fundamentally different from capitalist countries. Therefore, this trend can also prove that the foundation of the Soviet Union's domestic industry is gradually solidifying, and the need for foreign goods can be gradually reduced.

It is worth noting that the sharp decrease in Soviet Union's foreign trade is especially in terms of imports. In the ten months of 1934, the total imports were only 189.8 million rubles, compared with 291.2 million rubles in 1933, and even reached 597.1 million rubles in 1932. This means that in two years, the total amount of Soviet Union's imports has almost decreased by two-thirds. Similarly, it clearly proves that in the past two years, the Soviet Union's domestic industrial products have largely replaced foreign goods. As for the export part, in the ten months of 1934, the total amount was 343.8 million rubles, compared with 410.2 million rubles in 1933, and 461.4 million rubles in 1932. Although the total amount of Soviet Union's exports has decreased by 117.6 million rubles in the past two years, compared with the ratio of the decrease in total imports, it will be considered a small amount. On the other hand, in 1934, the export of silver and other precious metals was not included in the statistical table. According to the statistics of 1933, silver and other items accounted for 32.5 million rubles in the export category. Therefore, on the whole, the total amount of Soviet Union's exports in 1934 was not actually reduced by much.

In terms of foreign trade, the Soviet Union has become a country with a trade surplus in the past two years. In 1934, the trade surplus was 154 million rubles, and in 1933, the trade surplus was 119 million rubles. On the contrary, in 1932, the Soviet Union's trade deficit still accounted for 135.7 million rubles. Due to the trade surplus in the past two years and the large increase in gold production in the Soviet Union in recent years, not only can the foreign debts incurred by the Five-Year Plan be repaid on schedule, but also the price of the ruble in the international market is rising day by day. Up to this point, the difficult problem of Soviet Union's foreign trade has been completely resolved. At present, when ordering goods from other countries, the Soviet Union has put forward more favorable requirements regarding payment terms than ever before.

Although there have not been many changes in the Soviet Union's exports in 1934 in general, the significance is very different from the past. For example, a part of fully manufactured industrial products has been newly added to the exported goods. Although the number is not large, in the ten months of 1934, the total export of machinery (excluding agricultural machinery) was 1.4 million rubles, steel was 1.3 million rubles, steel products were 2.6 million rubles, and artificial fertilizers were 4.8 million rubles. This number is certainly not large, but it is enough to prove that the Soviet Union has gradually changed from an agricultural country to an industrial country. Naturally, the most important export product of the Soviet Union in the ten months of 1934 was still timber, with a total of 81.67 million rubles, an increase of about 13 million rubles compared with the export amount in the same period in 1933. The second was crude oil, with a total of 48.2 million rubles, a decrease of more than 16 million rubles compared with the same period in 1933. The third was tobacco, with a total of 28.96 million rubles, a decrease of about 8 million rubles compared with 1933. In addition, the total amount of grain was 18.28 million rubles, a decrease of more than 14 million rubles compared with 1933. The total amount of cotton was 18.82 million rubles, a decrease of about 7.5 million rubles compared with 1933. The total amount of flax was 16.02 million rubles, an increase of about 1.5 million rubles compared with 1933. The total amount of flour was 5.1 million rubles, an increase of about 2 million rubles compared with 1933. The total amount of cheese, etc. was 7.9 million rubles, a decrease of about 2 million rubles compared with 1933. This is the general overview of Soviet Union's export goods.

Regarding the Soviet Union's import sector, as mentioned above, it has also decreased by about 36% compared with 1933. The reason for this is naturally because in the early stage of the implementation of the Second Five-Year Plan in the Soviet Union, it had to purchase foreign industrial machinery in large quantities, so the total amount of imports was particularly large. By 1934, on the one hand, domestic industry gradually developed, and the machines produced in the country were sufficient to meet part of the domestic demand. On the other hand, the profound impact of the global economic panic still existed, and exports could not be developed as much as possible. Therefore, it was only possible to restrict the import sector to stabilize the market price of the Russian currency in the world market. This flexible foreign trade system has given the Soviet Union's economy an important guarantee. In the ten months of 1934, the total amount of machinery imported from foreign countries (excluding agricultural machinery) was 33.27 million rubles, while in the same period in 1933 it was 100.89 million rubles, and in 1932 it even reached 240.14 million rubles. The total amount of imported electrical appliances was 7.16 million rubles, 17.77 million rubles in 1933, and even 58.09 million rubles in 1932. The total amount of steel was 23.78 million rubles, which was still 40.8 million rubles in 1933. The total amount of other metals was 18.62 million rubles, which was 18.39 million rubles in 1933. The total amount of copper and iron products was 13.98 million rubles. In addition, the import amount of tea was 5.9 million rubles, livestock was 8.6 million rubles, tobacco was 5.7 million rubles, wool was 9.1 million rubles, etc.

As for the trade between the Soviet Union and other countries, in terms of country, the United Kingdom ranked first in terms of imports in 1934, accounting for 36.2 million rubles. In the same period in 1933, the United Kingdom's exports to the Soviet Union were only 9.3 million rubles. The second was Germany, accounting for 25.4 million rubles. In 1933, Germany's exports to the Soviet Union reached 114 million rubles. The sudden decrease in the trade volume in 1934 was naturally due to political reasons. The third was the United States. After the resumption of diplomatic relations between the United States and the Soviet Union, there were great hopes for commerce, but the result was not as expected. In 1934, the United States' exports to the Soviet Union amounted to 16.1 million rubles, only 1 million rubles more than in the same period in 1933 before the resumption of diplomatic relations. However, the Soviet Union's exports to the United States were only 10.8 million rubles in 1934, a decrease of 1.3 million rubles compared with 1933. This business result led to the suspension of debt negotiations between the United States and the Soviet Union recently, and the relations between the two countries have also tended to deteriorate. Originally, the resumption of diplomatic relations between the United States and the Soviet Union was mostly out of political motives, but Americans value profit and seem to attach particular importance to economic interests. When we see the trade figures between the United States and the Soviet Union in 1934, it is not difficult to understand the changes in the recent diplomatic relations between the two countries.

In short, judging from the Soviet Union's foreign trade in 1934, on the one hand, it shows that the domestic construction work has gradually reached a broad road, and it may be possible to catch up with the advanced industrial countries in Europe and the United States in the near future. On the other hand, precisely because of this, the conflict between the Soviet Union and other capitalist countries has become more acute, intensifying the attempt of various countries to jointly attack the Soviet Union. The European countries are preparing for war very urgently these days, and the scourge of war may break out at any time within a few years, and the Russian question is one of the most important fuse among them. (February 28th in Germany)

Japan's Activities in the Theatre of War 80

— (Japanese Correspondence)

The Ascendancy of the Restoration Movement and the Decline of Constitutional Politics

The high-sounding tones of good-neighborly diplomacy, amity with the United States, friendliness with the Soviet Union, cooperation with China, etc., are all sung loudly. Recently, the Chinese Eastern Railway has been successfully bought back. Judging from this situation, Japan's international diplomatic policy seems to be more inclined to peace. The Pacific Ocean can really be peaceful. Foreign Minister Hirota Koki's "moral diplomacy" should be worthy of its name. However, at the same time, we also see the active war preparations throughout Japan. The government-run military factories are working day and night, and all private factories that have a relatively close relationship with military supplies are making ten times the profit. Especially since February, major newspapers have invited generals from the army and navy who participated in the Russo-Japanese War to hold commemorative symposiums, extravagantly discussing the situation at the time of the war, elaborating on the war achievements, and encouraging the general public's fighting spirit.

The historical traces of war and peaceful diplomacy are juxtaposed, just as the Koishikawa Artillery Arsenal and the Tokyo Imperial University echo each other. The Tokyo Imperial University is where talents are cultivated, and scholarship and morality are lectured. The Koishikawa Artillery Arsenal, however, is continuously manufacturing tools for killing day and night, and the better the guns, the better. The idea is to kill more people, which is more in line with their original purpose. The entire political performance of Japan is also like this. More than 50 years have passed since the Meiji Restoration. Japan is a constitutional political country. The constitutional theory has been popular in schools for decades. The constitutional theory, which has never had a problem in the past, unexpectedly caused a great stir in this year's 67th Congress. Both the army and navy expressed their protest, and the spirit of the rule of law in parliamentary politics has obviously declined.

The decline of Japanese parliamentary politics is naturally also affected by the world's political relations. At the same time, the existing political parties have many undisguisable weaknesses. For example, the major bribery cases in the past have all involved key figures in the political parties, but this is not the most important reason. What deviates from the constitutional norm is the state of emergency—after the September 18th Incident, especially the May 15th Incident after Inukai's assassination—the military controlled the helm of the state of emergency. The higher the tune of the state of emergency, the greater the power of the military. The political parties simply have no room for activity. Everything has to listen to the guidance of the military. The military advocates taking the Emperor as the center, which is fundamentally different from the democratic thought of the parliament depending on the majority. Moreover, the established political parties, which are far away from the masses, bear the empty name of democracy and cannot get the support of the masses. Their decline is inevitable.

The middle class in Japan is very powerful, and its organizational strength is quite strong. Their beliefs are very solid, and their knowledge and ability have been trained to a considerable extent. They now constitute the center of gravity of Japanese society. These people are dissatisfied with the corruption of the upper class, dissatisfied with the political status quo, and especially dissatisfied with financial capital. Therefore, they support the military's policies and agree with everything the military does. The established political parties have lost the support of the masses and only have a false name.

"Peace" is an armed coat, a means for the military to borrow international diplomacy, and at the same time, it is also a trick for parliamentary politics and bureaucrats to cooperate. Let us take the example of military councillor Abe Nobuyuki's inspection of "Manchuria" on March 10 to prove the actual political trend in Japan. Originally, it was nothing unusual for Abe to go to the three northeastern provinces and comfort the troops in "Manchuria". What is noteworthy is that after Abe returned to Japan in April, Araki Sadao followed suit. (We all know that General Araki is the mastermind in the state of emergency and the leader of the young military officers.) His visit to "Manchuria" is by no means an ordinary tourist nature, and must contain major military and political implications. It is said that he will also go to North China to take a look. In May, the current Minister of the Army, Hayashi Senjuro, will follow in the footsteps of Abe and Araki to the four eastern provinces, also saying that he is inspecting and comforting the troops in "Manchuria". It is rare for the current Minister of the Army to go abroad to inspect in Japan, and it has a special meaning to go to North China and other places. The Japanese military strategist General Watanabe Jotaro (currently a military councillor) will go to the four northeastern provinces after Minister of the Army Hayashi Senjuro returns to China. The last person to go is General Matsui Iwane (a China expert in the army). On the surface, they all say that they are inspecting and comforting the troops. All the military councillors in the army have to go to "Manchuria" once. The missions they bear are roughly the same, and the internal meaning is equally important. In this period of decline of constitutional politics and the leap of military power, peace is probably placed under the military sword. (March 23rd in Tokyo)

Bandits Spring Up in the War Zone, Yutian's Illegal Militia Flees to Fengrun and Jixian, and Feng Shoupeng's Mutinous Troops are Defeated and Flee to Shunyi 81

Beiping Correspondence: The security of the war zone is actually insufficient due to the limited number and weapons of the security teams. In addition, some security teams and special police were temporarily reorganized from the old troops of puppet army officers such as Li Jichun and Shi Yousan due to special relations. There were often incidents of colluding with bandits and illegal militias to oppress the local people, which led to the inability to eliminate the scattered bandits, resulting in the inability to maintain security. After the authorities and the Japanese side agreed on measures to clean up the war zone, the first step was to transfer and reorganize Sun Yuchen's security team in Yutian and Feng Shoupeng's special police team, and reorganize the illegal militia in Yutian. However, after Feng's troops were transferred, more than 300 people mutinied and became bandits, looting everywhere. The illegal militia under Wang Chengzhu also refused to be reorganized. At the same time, scattered bandits everywhere began to harass. Feng Shoupeng's mutinous troops once harassed Miyun. After being besieged by the security team, they crossed Huairou and Shunyi from Miyun County on the 24th and fled to Lisui Town. They were intercepted by the security team there and fled east again. After passing through Sanhe County, they fled to Yanjiao Town near Tongxian County, attempting to incite the former Sun Yuchen's security team, which had been transferred from Yutian to the area. Yesterday, they were blocked and suppressed by the security team, and most of them were defeated. The remaining 70 or so people formed a small group and fled back to Wanggezhuang in Shunyi County today (26th). The Shunyi County security team is currently besieging them. The authorities originally took a lenient attitude towards Wang Chengzhu's illegal militia in Ya Hongqiao, Yutian, and reorganized them. However, the militia refused to be reorganized, plotted against the authorities, secretly colluded with Feng Shoupeng's mutinous troops and bandits, and hired a Japanese man, Noda, as an advisor. The Jimei District Commissioner's Office sent personnel to inform them several times, but they always disobeyed. To prevent this from happening, the authorities sent the security team under Zhou Yuying, stationed in Yutian, to take surveillance actions in the Niugezhuang and Gaoqiao areas at dawn on the 24th. The troops took surveillance actions around Ya Hongqiao. The troops deployed defenses around Ya Hongqiao and attacked the security team. The two sides made contact at noon yesterday (25th). Zhou's troops, believing that the troops were resisting orders, bravely advanced and suppressed them. After five hours of fierce fighting, many bandits were killed. The bandits were unable to resist and retreated in all directions. That night, Zhou's troops occupied Ya Hongqiao. In this battle, four members of Zhou's security team were killed and more than a dozen were injured. The bandit troops originally had more than a thousand people. Now, in addition to those killed and scattered, most of them fled to Jingyu in Zunhua County this morning. Another group of about 300 people fled east, with the intention of fleeing to Fengrun. Zhou's troops are currently tracking and pursuing them, and have informed the security teams of Zunhua and Fengrun to intercept them. On the 24th, the bandits found in the second district of Jixian have been eliminated. Thirty-nine bandits were captured, and twenty-eight guns were seized. The bandit leader, Zhang Hanmin, was also arrested. The bandits were from the disbanded militia in Yutian, who had been in contact with Feng Shoupeng's troops, oppressing the local people. When Feng's troops were transferred and the militia was disbanded, they became bandits. A few days ago, more than 300 bandits fled to Zunhua from Ran County via Sheshentai. They were blocked and suppressed by the Zunhua security team and have now fled to Qian'an County. The Aoyu District security team is currently besieging them. This time, bandits have harassed various places in the war zone. There are about 2,000 people, and they have fled to six or seven counties. The bandit troops are fully armed and have weapons such as machine guns. The security teams are too small in number, the defense area is vast, and the military strength is extremely weak. In addition, the weapons are limited, making it difficult to suppress them. When Feng Shoupeng's mutinous troops fled to Miyun a few days ago, they consulted with the Japanese army in the Gubeikou area and carried light machine guns to suppress the bandits. As a result, they were only allowed to carry six machine guns, and they could only be used when necessary. The authorities believe that the bandits are springing up and causing trouble, and it is not enough to secure the region without eliminating them. Yin Rugeng, the administrative commissioner of the Jimei District, went to Tianjin from Ping a few days ago to discuss suppression measures with the provincial government and to negotiate everything with the Tianjin Japanese Garrison Headquarters and the Shanhaiguan Special Service Agency Chief Iga. This morning, Yin, accompanied by Iga and the staff officer Omoki of the Japanese Garrison in Tianjin, went to Tangshan from Tianjin and then to Yutian to handle the suppression of bandits and the reorganization of the militia. After completing his official duties in Yutian, he will go to the Yanjiao area to inspect the situation after the transfer of the security team. (March 26th)

Guantai Closure Stops Work, Actively Preparing Materials, Hoping for Closure in Two Months 82

Kaifeng Correspondence: Since the central government ordered the change of the agency in charge of the Guantai project and stopped waiting for materials, the current work relief group in charge has appointed special commissioners for transportation, material purchase, accounting, affairs, material factory, and engineering office, and is stepping up preparations for various materials and various equipment. It is estimated that more than 200 ships have been requisitioned from Wuzhi, Sishui, Guangwu, Gongxian, and Kaifeng, and dozens more from Puyang and Changtan have been telegraphed to be escorted to Guan immediately. Shandong is also requisitioning at the same time. For stone transportation, Longhai and Pinghan have dispatched vehicles, which will start transporting on the 25th and 26th respectively. The Jinpu Railway has also specially dispatched three trains to assist in the handling. One train will depart from Heshangqiao Station on the Pinghan Railway, and the other from Xuzhou Station on the Longhai Railway, transporting large quantities of stone from Xingshan and Dahu Mountain, respectively, to Lanfeng Station, where they will be transferred by rail trucks. Four hundred extra carts will be hired and transported in shifts day and night, and special transport ships will be prepared on the opposite bank of Guantai to be loaded as they arrive and delivered directly to the Guantai mouth. It is said that a total of 7,000 city squares of stone have been ordered, which is about 30,000 cubic meters. However, the three-way transportation is calculated on the basis of three trains arriving at Lanfeng Station every day, and it will still be difficult to collect them all in about 20 days. In addition, 2,000 city squares of old and new stone materials stored by the Pinggong Institute of the Yu River Affairs Bureau will be borrowed. A few million catties of kaoliang materials have been purchased on behalf of the Zheng County Commissioner's Office, and one million catties have been purchased in Kaifeng, and tens of thousands of catties have been shipped. Forty thousand catties have also been settled in Chenliu, and they are all being shipped. Three million catties of willow branches have been settled in Liuyuankou and Chenqiaokou in Kaifeng. Hemp bags, lead wire, iron anchors, etc. have all been purchased and loaded in Shanghai and will arrive in Lanfeng in batches starting today (27th). More than 200,000 catties of hemp have been purchased and transported, and personnel were also sent to Hankou last night to purchase a large quantity of linen, which is scheduled to be shipped here within a few days. Before the arrival of large quantities of materials, special attention will be paid to the defense work of the projects that have been done. According to Kong Xiangrong, we will take the opportunity to advance the closure after the manpower and materials are collected, and it is expected that the closure will be completed in two months. (27th)

Fujian Army Captures Zhao'an Bandit Stronghold; Meizhou is an Important Nest of Pirates and a Key Area for Planting Opium 83

Shantou Correspondence: Zhao'an is remotely located on the edge of southern Fujian, with many coastal mountains. It borders Raoping in eastern Guangdong. For more than a decade, it has often been an area where pirates appear. Meizhou Township, in particular, is a major den of pirates. Its range of looting extends as far as Fuzhou, Xiamen, Jiangxi, Raoping, Chenghai, Shantou, Taiwan, Hong Kong, and Macau. The magnitude of its power can be imagined. The terrain of Meizhou is located in the southwest of Zhao'an, with mountains behind and the sea in front. Rivers run through it, and the harbors are curved and intricate, with grotesque rocks standing out and dangerous shapes. The population of the entire township is about 30,000, and there are more than 10,000 people in the surrounding 300-odd villages, large and small. Because they are oppressed by bandits and coerced, they are driven to engage in a life of robbery all day long, committing crimes. Fathers pass it on to their sons, almost considering it a legitimate profession.

In addition to being forced to engage in robbery, the people of Meizhou and the surrounding 300-odd villages also engage in opium cultivation as their main occupation. The locals never ask about farming throughout the year, only wishing for a good harvest of poppies. Opium exports reach 200,000 to 300,000 taels to as much as 500,000 to 600,000 taels per month. Each tael is worth two to three yuan. Considering only the income from opium cultivation each year, it reaches more than ten million yuan, not counting the proceeds from robbery. The most opium is shipped to Shanghai and Southeast Asia, followed by Chaozhou and Xiamen. The opium shipped to Chaozhou is mostly smuggled from Zhao'an into Rao, and then distributed to various places, thus avoiding the collection of special taxes. Therefore, its price is cheaper than opium shipped from other places. Years ago, the Chao-Mei Anti-Opium Bureau specially set up a special investigation team to investigate and crack down on tax-evading Meizhou opium. Since then, Meizhou opium shipped to Chaozhou is willing to pay taxes. However, because Chaozhou needs a lot of opium, the shipment of Meizhou opium to Chaozhou does not decrease because of taxation. In Meizhou, the four major companies are the giants in operating opium, followed by the six shareholders. Those who boast of wealth often claim to have property of a certain number of *dong* (冬, *dong* is a container for storing opium, shaped like a large vat, which can hold sixteen *dan* of opium, called one *dong*). As for the defense of bandit dens, the Meizhou pirates are divided into six major gangs, plus more than a dozen small gangs. The six major gangs are the most powerful and especially rampant. Each major gang has from one thousand to three thousand people, and the small gangs also have hundreds of people. They divide into land and sea routes to carry out robbery. Every day, they seize dozens of ransom tickets and rob more than ten ships, all imprisoned in the township to await ransom. The gangs often compete with each other because of the relationship between tickets and stolen goods. The entire township is divided into three major defense lines. The bandit nests of each gang and the places where the ransom tickets are imprisoned are the inner defense line. Various places in the township are the second defense line. Anyone who discovers a ransom ticket escaping, regardless of which gang or person, can kill it on the spot. The outside of the township and the harbor are the first defense line to prevent the army from encircling and suppressing them and attacks from other villages. There are many underground camp caves in the mountains, which are connected by underground tunnels dug from the township. In addition, ditches are dug in important places on the land route into the township. Furthermore, mountain torrents are gathered and stored on the mountains, and diverted into pits and ditches. In case of emergency, the mountain torrents are immediately released to block traffic, so as to defend against foreign invaders. Because of the meticulous defense, the Meizhou bandits have been rampant for more than ten years, and the government troops have never been able to do anything about it.

This time, Fujian Province is strictly enforcing the opium ban and forcibly eradicating opium seedlings. The Meizhou bandits regard opium as their lifeline and strive to avoid the strict ban. At first, they entrusted Mr. Zhang, a neighbor who had served as a division commander, with 300,000 yuan to lobby, but Zhang refused. The Meizhou tyrants then used Zhang's village as a threat. Zhang had no choice but to instruct his wife to lobby, but it was too late, and the government did not approve it. The people of Meizhou then advocated resisting the inspection and prohibition. The defense army stationed in Yunxiao Zhao'an, under the order of the Zhangzhou Pacification Office, led a regiment to Meizhou to eradicate opium. Each district of Meizhou then joined forces to resist, and released mountain torrents into the ditches, submerging the roads. Later, reinforcements used ships to provide support. After seven days of fierce fighting, the bandits were defeated and all escaped to the back mountains through underground tunnels. Only dozens of people were captured, and more than 100 ransom tickets were rescued. More than 100 ransom tickets were drowned and starved to death by the water. After the township was broken, the army implemented a clean-up, and seized more than 8 million taels of opium, including those hidden for more than ten years, all of which were burned. Now the township is garrisoned by the army, and most of the villagers have fled outside and dare not return to their hometown. Some of them have joined gangs and gone up the mountain to become bandits. From now on, the residents and travelers in the area along the border of Guangdong and Fujian should be able to obtain safety. (24th)

Northern Anhui Tea Industry Business Tax—Bureau Established Three Days Before Qingming Festival to Handle Matters 84

Anqing Correspondence: Anhui is a tea-producing province, and tea taxes have always been a reliable source of income. In recent years, the Department of Finance has adopted a contractor system. Every year at the end of the lunar year, it relies on the guarantee deposits of tea tax contractors to embellish the accounts. However, last year, the counties of Huizhou suffered from the intrusion of Jiangxi bandits, and the order was disturbed. Most of those who had bid for tea taxes hesitated. Although the counties in northern Anhui are safer than those in southern Anhui, the tax amount is slightly lower. As a result, the Department of Finance changed to a commissioned system, and only yesterday (26th) did it officially announce the directors of the tea industry business tax bureaus in the counties of northern and southern Anhui. Yang Mianzhong, the director of the Department of Finance, specially convened the directors of the commissioned bureaus yesterday afternoon to instruct them on everything, and urged them to prepare to depart quickly and establish bureaus to collect taxes three days before the Qingming Festival. It is also heard that the Department of Finance plans to set up four inspection bureaus at key locations in each bureau to specialize in inspecting the tax collection situation of each bureau. The candidates for the directors of each bureau who have been announced are: Jia Mingjiu in Zhidong, Xu Tao in Xiuyi, Zhang Shouquan in Maotan Factory, Zhu Tianxiu in Qimen, Yao Dapeng in Jingtai, Zhu Baoru in Mabou and Jianlianghekou, Zhao Yunchang in Huoshan and Jianguanjiabu, Xu Zhiqin in Shexian, Guang Sipu in Xuanlang, Huang Zichun in Balitan, Sun Daishi in Tongshi, and Zhao Tongfang in Qilihe. Floating Corpse Discovered North of Xiuye Bridge 87

A male floating corpse, about forty years old, was discovered in the river north of Xiuye Bridge in the city this morning. He was wearing a gray cotton robe, lined with a yuan-colored cotton jacket, gray cotton pants, and rubber shoes. It is not known where the corpse came from. The town police reported to the county court prosecutor's office, and officials went to the scene for an examination. It was determined that there were no injuries. Because there were no family members to claim it, the town police were ordered to prepare a coffin and wait for a public announcement to claim it.

Wuxi Appeals for Exemption from Silk Cocoon Tax 88

The silk factory trade association of this county believes that factory silk in our country is a major export. In recent years, affected by the devaluation and dumping of Japanese silk, the silk market has plummeted, and exports have been sharply reduced. Compared with the heyday, it only accounts for 15%. Xidi has always been a sericulture production area. In recent years, due to the tragic decline in the silk market, the silk factories have suffered huge losses, so the price of cocoons has been lowered, and farmers have no profit in raising silkworms. They have all turned mulberry fields into rice fields, resulting in a reduction in the output of dried cocoons in Xidi. The raw materials needed by various factories have to be purchased from provinces such as Zhejiang, Shandong, Anhui, and Hubei and transported to Xixiao for silk reeling. However, in places where customs are set up in various provinces, they often forcibly collect silk scraps or cocoon shell taxes on dried cocoons. At this critical moment for the survival of the silk industry, illegal taxation by the customs increases the cost of factory silk. If it is not stopped immediately, it will inevitably lead to the complete bankruptcy of silk factories across the country. Therefore, yesterday, they specially presented a report to the Ministry of Finance, requesting permission to instruct the competent authorities of relevant provinces and various customs to investigate and clarify that all donations and taxes involving silk cocoons should be exempted. At the same time, they also submitted reports to the Ministry of Transportation and the Ministry of Railways, requesting that the Beijing-Shanghai, Hangzhou-Tianjin-Pukou, Ping-Han, Long-Hai, and Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Administrations, as well as the China Merchants Bureau's shipping bureaus, be instructed to give preferential treatment to the freight of dry cocoons by halving the cost, in order to reduce costs.

The barber industry in this county recently decided to implement the issue of carrying pole permits before the 15th of this month, but the barber shops outside Nanmen unanimously opposed it, causing disputes. Yesterday, members of the barber industry association, Gu Yunqing, Zhou Gaisheng, and Sha Licheng, convened a meeting to discuss mediation methods. They were taken to the First Public Security Bureau. After questioning by Bureau Member Min, they were transferred to the General Bureau for interrogation.

In addition, the tomb of Wu Niansheng, east of Zhangtang Bridge near Hongshengli in the eighth district, was also robbed by more than a dozen bandits. They also tied up the tomb keeper, Lu Kang Er, and blinded both eyes. As a result, more than ten shi of white rice were robbed. Yesterday, the competent Seventh Public Security Bureau was reported and requested to investigate and arrest the escaped bandits.

All Circles in Shanghai Held Memorial Meeting for Huanghuagang Martyrs Yesterday; More Than 500 People Attended at the Folk Education Center; All Agencies and Schools Had Holidays and Flew Flags at Half-Mast 97

Yesterday was the anniversary of the Huanghuagang Martyrs Revolution. At 9:00 a.m., all circles in Shanghai held a memorial meeting at the Folk Education Center. Jiang Hao, a member of the Municipal Party Committee, reported on the course and significance of the March 29th Revolution. Zhu Xuefan also gave a speech. All agencies and schools in the city had a holiday for one day, and flags were flown at half-mast everywhere to express condolences. The details are recorded as follows:

Attending Representatives

Jiang Hao of the Municipal Party Committee, Chen Kecheng of the Municipal Government, Huang Zaoxiong of the Municipal Education Association, Yu Zhenhui of the Municipal Agricultural Association, Zhu Xuefan of the General Labor Union, Ke Ganchen of the South Municipal Council, Luo Weixiong of the Garrison Command (the above are the presidium), Gao Wuhe of the Shanghai First Special Zone Court, Yao Changjiong of the Municipal Education Bureau, Xie Shouquan of the Defense Committee, Chen Songchun of the Folk Education Center, Dong Chongshan of the Second Special Zone Court, Dai Baojun of the International Telecommunications Bureau, Wang Zongjian of the Jianghai Customs, Hu Tianseng of the New Movement Promotion Association, Ren Bin of the Tooth and Bone Industry Union, Yu Yaoqiu of the South Goods Industry Union, and more than 500 representatives of primary and secondary schools such as Zhengfeng Minli Jianguo Shangwen.

Chairman's Report

After the ceremony was performed as usual, Chairman Jiang Hao first gave a report, saying: Today, all circles in Shanghai are holding a memorial for the Huanghuagang Martyrs Revolution. This is a necessary stage in the revolutionary process. At that time, the revolutionary team led by the Premier occasionally failed in revolutionary actions and were sincerely terrified. However, the Premier still adhered to the spirit of perseverance and began to plan this great revolutionary action. At that time, the Premier and the revolutionary pioneers discussed launching in Guangzhou and seizing the southwest as a base for the revolution, and decided to take responsibility for carrying it out separately. The Premier went overseas to raise funds. Overseas comrades were happy to follow. At one time, they raised about 200,000 yuan. Huang Keqiang planned the military launch in Hong Kong. At first, progress was slow due to financial difficulties. Later, the Premier raised a large sum of money, and immediately purchased weapons and sent comrades to secretly infiltrate Guangzhou. At that time, the Qing government was already aware of this, so it was heavily guarded. However, the comrades still spared no effort and painstakingly made active arrangements in Guangzhou. In the meantime, I don't know how many twists and turns were taken. On March 29, they used white cloth wrapped around their arms as a signal and attacked in three routes. Huang Keqiang personally led his comrades to attack the Governor's Office, but all three routes temporarily failed due to the disparity in numbers. After the investigation, 72 revolutionary martyrs were sacrificed in this disaster. Although the event was unsuccessful, the righteousness of their uprising and the heroism of their death were enough to move the gods and frighten the enemy. Later, the comrades buried the seventy-two martyrs in Huanghuagang, hence the name. In this revolutionary process, we deeply feel that the success of the revolution is a curved line and must go through many hardships before it can be achieved. However, we must go to it with a spirit of great fearlessness. Today, China's national fortune is still difficult. We should follow the spirit of the martyrs and build the Chinese nation. Now the central government is working hard on unification and construction to enrich national power. If we can be united from top to bottom, the rejuvenation is bound to be promising.

Main Points of the Speech

Then, Zhu Xuefan gave a speech, saying that the Battle of Huanghuagang was entirely for the purpose of equality for the Chinese nation, equality of civil rights, and equality of economy. The spirit of struggle and sacrifice of the martyrs is truly admirable. Today, China is still in a dangerous period. In the future, we should (1) gather China's strength to save the nation, save the masses, and save the country; (2) save the country and save the people should start from ourselves. As the ancients said, everyone is responsible for the rise and fall of the country. I hope to encourage each other.

Memorial Slogans

(1) Inherit the spirit of sacrifice and struggle of the revolutionary martyrs; (2) Unite the comrades of the party; (3) Complete the unfinished legacy of the revolutionary martyrs; (4) Support peaceful unification; (5) Support the revolutionary leader; (6) Strive for production and construction; (7) Eliminate the remnant bandits; (8) The spirit of the revolutionary martyrs will never die; (9) Long live the Three Principles of the People; (10) Long live the Chinese Kuomintang; (11) Long live the Republic of China.

Four Groups Hosted a Banquet for Hart Last Night; Lin Kanghou Delivered a Welcome Speech; Hart is Scheduled to Go to Hangzhou Today 98

Mr. and Mrs. Hart, the Economic Minister of the Dutch East Indies, are traveling in China and have been welcomed by all circles in Shanghai. In order to express the feeling of contact, the National Federation of Commerce, the Institute of International Studies, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, and the International Trade Association and other four groups, specially at 7:30 last night, held a banquet at the Bank Guild Club. A reporter from the Central News Agency specially investigated and reported the details as follows:

Guests at the Banquet: The banquet was held at 7:30 last night. The hosts included Wen Lanting, Lin Kanghou, Chen Riping, Zeng Xianyuan, and Gu Huaibing, representatives of the National Federation of Commerce; Chen Zhezheng, Guo Bingwen, and Tu Chuyu, representatives of the Institute of International Studies; Ke Ganchen and Zheng Zenan, representatives of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; Chen Changtong, Pan Guangjiong, and Shao Zenghua, representatives of the International Trade Association; and Yuan Ludeng, Xu Xinliu, Yu Qiaqing, Qian Chengxu, Chen Guangfu, He Dekui, Xu Peikun, Gan Haifeng, He Bingxian, Song Yizhong, Gao Dajing were invited to accompany them, and Lin Kanghou was elected as the chairman.

Representatives Delivered Speeches: During the session, Chairman Lin Kanghou delivered a welcome speech on behalf of the four groups, saying: Today, the National Federation of Commerce, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the China International Trade Association, and the Institute of International Studies are welcoming Mr. Hart, the Economic Minister of the Dutch East Indies, and have prepared a humble feast to welcome Mr. Hart. We are very honored that Mr. Hart has taken the time to come. Tracing back to the friendly relations between China and the Netherlands, although geographically separated by Europe and Asia, the exchanges have been very early. In particular, the Dutch East Indies is adjacent to China, and the relationship is very close. The East Indies began to belong to the Netherlands in the 16th century, and in the Jin Dynasty in China, about 1,030 years ago, there was a monk named Faxian who returned to China from India and passed through Java. At that time, Chinese people had already lived there. Later, they continued to develop to various islands, and the number of Chinese people traveling south also increased from generation to generation. Until recently, the total number of Chinese people living on the islands of the East Indies was about 1.1 million. Initially, the islands of the East Indies only had scholars, and culture and commerce had not yet been developed. The Chinese worked hard and intentionally operated, and after being governed by the Netherlands, they cooperated to create the East Indies of today. To this day, the Chinese occupy a huge economic position in the East Indies. Therefore, looking back on the past and speculating on the future, the prosperity and decline of the East Indies are closely related to the Chinese. A few years ago, the East Indies was affected by the global economic downturn, and the market plummeted. The business of the Chinese was also greatly affected. I think Mr. Hart, as the Economic Minister of the Dutch East Indies, must have a plan in mind for how to promote the commerce between China and the Netherlands in the future, and how to restore the prosperity of the East Indies. This time, he came to China to investigate, and he should research the above two questions and reach a stable position. I, on behalf of the four groups, offer a toast to Mr. Hart and hope that Mr. Hart will come forward and give us guidance.

Mr. Hart's Reply: Mr. Hart stood up and replied, saying: This time, I came to China to travel in a personal capacity. I am very grateful for the warm hospitality of all of you and the authorities of your country. When I passed through Hong Kong, I was also welcomed by the people of your country, which shows the friendly relations between China and the Netherlands. Your country is a country with thousands of years of culture, and the relationship between the two countries began very early. The number of Chinese people living in the Dutch East Indies is very large. In terms of historical relations, it has indeed benefited us a lot in cultural progress. At this time of economic downturn, all industries are declining. I am very willing to cooperate with your compatriots to seek development. I have known many people in your country for the past 15 years, and our relationship is harmonious. In particular, the working spirit of your people has always been admired. I wish all of you here good health.

Going to Hangzhou Today: Then, the chairman, guests, and hosts discussed the current international economic downturn and ways to remedy it. It ended at about 9:00 p.m. A reporter from the Central News Agency learned that Mr. and Mrs. Hart will go to Hangzhou for sightseeing this afternoon. In one or two days, they will go to Beijing to visit President Wang, Minister of Finance Kong, and Chief Secretary Chen, and then go to Peiping for sightseeing. It is expected that they will stay in Peiping for four days and then return to the country via Shanghai to resume their duties.

Soong Tzu-wen Appointed as Director of the Bank of China; Close Cooperation Among the Three Major Banks Has No Connection to Monetary Policy; Increase in Government Capital Does Not Change the Independent Nature of the Bank of China 99

Kong Xiangxi Speaks. National News Agency, 24/3/29, Local News: Finance Minister Kong told a National News Agency reporter that the increase in capital and the addition of directors to the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications are part of a long-held government policy to strengthen these three banks. Minister Kong also stated that in light of the general economic downturn in recent years, and the further difficulties resulting from recent US banking policies, the three banks should strive to cooperate in order to cope with the local market situation. Mr. T.V. Soong and others have been appointed by the government as directors of the Bank of China, and Mr. Zhang Jia'ao has been appointed as one of the vice presidents of the Central Bank. As for the Bank of Communications, there will be no other changes besides the government's additional appointment of official shareholder directors. Furthermore, the above-mentioned changes are purely to facilitate the cooperation of the three banks and to solidify the foundation of our country's banking industry. Minister Kong also declared that the close cooperation of these three major banks has no connection whatsoever with the government's monetary policy. The three banks will each maintain their inherent original status. Minister Kong solemnly declared again that the cooperation of the three banks will greatly benefit the government's intention to regulate the market, because although the market situation has improved somewhat recently, it is still hoped that our country's banking system can be further improved.

Soong Tzu-wen Speaks. A National News Agency reporter recently met with Mr. T.V. Soong, a standing committee member of the Economic Commission, and was informed that he had indeed been appointed as a director of the Bank of China. The government's measures for the three banks are to increase their strength and promote their close cooperation for substantial progress, so that they can fully exert their power to serve society. This is a long-planned scheme since the establishment of the National Government. From now on, the three banks together will be more effective in regulating the market and resolving various financial difficulties. As for the Bank of China itself, in addition to the increase in government capital, it remains completely independent in nature. Its business scope and all the privileges granted by the government will continue to be handled according to the old regulations, without any changes. Mr. Soong believes that the government's move is indeed a natural step to solidify the foundation of the domestic banking industry.

Bank of China Holds Shareholders' Meeting Today to Discuss the Issue of Increasing Government Shares; Original Articles of Association to be Amended; Candidates for Chairman of the Board Will Also Be Discussed 100

Central News Agency reports that the 100 million yuan financial bonds issued by the Ministry of Finance have been designated to allocate a portion for the shares in the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications. The Bank of China and the Bank of Communications were originally jointly operated by government and private capital. Now that government shares have increased, there should be corresponding changes in the distribution of their organization. The shareholders' meeting of the Bank of China is scheduled to be held at 1:00 p.m. today, and all issues will be brought up for discussion.

Number of Directors and Supervisors Will Be Increased

The capital of the Bank of China was originally 25 million yuan, with 20 million yuan being private shares and 5 million yuan being government shares. Therefore, the distribution of directors and supervisors was in a ratio of five to one between the private and government sides. There were fifteen private shareholder directors, three government shareholder directors, five private shareholder supervisors, and one government shareholder supervisor. This time, the government allocated an additional 25 million yuan in capital, bringing the total to 30 million yuan. Therefore, the ratio of government to private shares will be three to two, and the number of government directors and supervisors will also be increased.

Incumbent Directors and Supervisors Will Not Be Re-elected

At today's shareholders' meeting, the matter of adding government shares will be formally submitted for approval. After approval, the number of shareholder rights on the government side will increase. As for the incumbent directors and supervisors, they will not be re-elected because their terms have not expired. However, the government will add to the number of directors and supervisors in accordance with the law by the Ministry of Finance. The candidates for the additional positions are currently under consideration and will be convened for a meeting of directors and supervisors after a decision is made. It is possible that the current chairman of the board, Li Fuxun, will be asked to resign.

Candidates for Chairman of the Board Will Be Discussed

The candidates for chairman of the board and general manager will be discussed at today's shareholders' meeting. Although the current chairman of the board, Li... and general manager Zhang Gongquan have not made any definite statements, it is feared that Mr. Zhang will find it difficult to manage both roles, as he has already been appointed as the vice president of the Central Bank. Mr. Zhang himself is currently considering whether to accept the new appointment. If he accepts the new appointment, he will inevitably resign from his position as the general manager of the Bank of China.

Original Articles of Association Will Also Be Amended

The original articles of association will also be submitted for discussion at today's shareholders' meeting. Since the Bank of China has increased government shares, there are several points that must be amended in terms of content. After the articles of association are amended, the process will proceed according to the new articles of association. Therefore, the matter of increasing government shares is the focus of discussion at today's meeting. Once the issue of government shares is resolved, other issues can proceed smoothly.

American Aircraft Engineer Mr. Dikeman Arrives in Shanghai to Study China's Aviation Industry 107

Full Text of the Sassoon Plan (Continued) 108

There is also a suggestion, created by some parties, to adopt a new currency based on the British pound to replace the existing currency. Silver is still the most suitable medium for foreign exchange in China, and the difficulties we encounter are mostly local rather than widespread. Therefore, we should not consider abandoning the silver standard. I have said this before.

What the United States is concerned about is the excess of both currency and credit, while what Shanghai is concerned about is the deficiency of both currency and credit. Using inflation to expand currency will inevitably cause harm, but if currency expansion can be achieved in a stable manner, the immediate benefits should be considerable.

Therefore, I suggest that there is something worth considering: if a British pound loan can be found, can it be used for the above-mentioned purposes, as a reserve for a kind of subsidiary currency or substitute currency, rather than for the dubious purpose of stabilizing or controlling foreign exchange? As for the issue of collateral for this kind of loan, it is of course still to be discussed, but what I want to say is the possibility of how much benefit a smaller debt can produce.

How much the amount is is extremely important. I don't want to estimate it. What I suggest is that if China can obtain a considerable amount of British pound loans, it can beneficially and safely issue a kind of banknote, with British pounds as collateral, and circulate it in the market together with the existing silver coins.

At first glance, this move does not seem to have any special benefits, and Shanghai may not have much demand for this kind of pound note. But if we consider it a little, this pound note can obviously have various uses in daily commerce. Let us first talk about the import problem. Currently, importers, if they cannot find a way to keep their capital in foreign currency before their imports are sold, must take the risk of foreign exchange at the time of import, and there is often the risk of loss on foreign exchange. If they do not want to lose, they must not sell the goods in hand, otherwise, they must go beyond the scope of the merchant's true business and hedge into exchange bills to protect themselves and prevent the exchange rate from rising. But this move can also allow competitors to seize their transactions with lower selling prices.

If exporters can not only not settle the exchange rate for the foreign currency cost of their goods, but also sell them in the same foreign currency, they do not take the risk of foreign exchange and can always know exactly how much profit they can get.

The above method can be applied to all importers who purchase goods from British pound countries and avoid the need to hedge into exchange bills. However, importers who purchase goods from other countries still need to buy exchange bills.

The claim that Shanghai should buy goods in British pounds over the counter seems bizarre at first glance, but in reality, it is something that often exists in the purchase and sale of many imported goods. Retail stores change their prices at any time according to the exchange rate. On the buyer's side, they are actually buying goods in foreign currency. If the goods are sold in British pounds and the buyer pays in pound notes, then the buyer may not need to use silver dollars at all.

The people of Shanghai may as well purchase pound notes or open British pound credit accounts in banks. Whether buying a bottle of whiskey, a foreign novel, a pair of foreign leather shoes, or a can of tobacco, they can all use it uniformly. The price will of course be subject to changes in the source. The price that the consumer pays in British pounds will not change from time to time.

Now assume that imported goods can be priced and paid in British pounds, then importers may as well pay their customs duties in this new currency. This is also one of the greatest uses of the new currency. The exchange rate between customs gold and local general silver dollars is determined daily, and the exchange rate between pound notes and silver dollars can also be determined in this way. In fact, given the current silver price, I do not see why customs gold should not be abolished and replaced with British pounds.

The Ministry of Finance is not more disadvantageous than before, because the British pounds of customs revenue can still be used to repay foreign debt and overseas uses without any difficulty. As for purely domestic needs, such as clearing domestic bonds, the situation is no different from today when customs gold is collected. Export taxes can still be collected in silver.

If we consider how much of the goods purchased and services enjoyed in Shanghai come from foreign countries, we will see that the use of this new currency is not limited to buying and selling imported goods. Take hotels as an example. A large part of its expenses are attributed to overseas. The carpets, curtains, knives, etc. it places need to be replaced at any time. The alcoholic beverages it prepares must come from overseas. The employees it hires need to be paid in foreign currency. A large part of the hotel's revenue comes from the expenses of travelers coming to Shanghai. It is the wish of tourists to be able to avoid the difficulties of local foreign exchange. If a hotel cannot pay for its imports in Shanghai pound notes and set its prices, it will be more advantageous to convert most of its accounts into British pounds. If so, the demand for silver dollars can be eased a little. In practice, it may be necessary to supply some smaller representative currency systems. This substitute currency may as well be provided by the municipal council, such as the auxiliary currency issued by the city of Paris during the European War for small change.

Shanghai is not short of salaried classes who pay their full or part of their salaries in British pounds. They are very willing to receive their salaries in this new currency and avoid the labor of conversion.

Those who take leave to return home can carry this pound note with them. This currency will eventually become a kind of internationally circulating currency, like five-pound notes and one-pound notes.

I do not mean that this new currency should be a permanent currency in China, nor that it can be applied to other parts of China outside of Shanghai. However, this note will eventually have some circulation in other ports. I am only making this suggestion on a trial basis, as a possible way to expand currency without inflating currency, so as to overcome the difficult times we are currently encountering. Something that does not need to be imagined is that this currency will be more popular than ordinary currency for hoarding. If so, it is also beneficial to the public, because it can free up more silver dollars to circulate in the market, and this silver dollar must always be the main currency of China.

Regarding the agency for implementing this plan, I would like to briefly describe its method, but I admit that my opinion on this matter is quite fluid and not resolute at the current stage.

It seems that a committee can be organized to handle the issuance of pound notes, and the members of this committee should be representatives of the Ministry of Finance and Chinese and foreign banks.

The British pound loan obtained is handed over to the control of this committee, and the committee can then sell pound notes equal to the amount of the debt.

This currency may flow back to London after a certain period of time and take out the cash. In any case, since the debt is received, attention must be paid to payment. At this time, this committee should have received the cash capital from the sale of this kind of pound note.

This kind of pound note cannot be allowed for speculation, so the silver dollars received must be hedged out in the long term to protect them. At the same time, this silver dollar can be lent to banks for a certain period of time, so that the silver funds can be eased.

If the number of people who pay to purchase this pound note continues to increase, exceeding the total amount of the debt, then this committee must remit the cash capital it has received in order to reduce the overdraft in other areas. I can say that there is no need for bankers to say that, according to the plan I have said, considerable profits can be obtained to pay for printing and other expenses, and net profits can be obtained in the total allocation.

In summary, if this pound note can circulate freely, then this plan can first increase currency, and second can expand credit, because since there are pound coins, British pound loans based on Shanghai assets can be used freely, and banks will definitely be prepared to release British pound overdrafts.

My suggestion is to avoid interfering with China's existing currency, not only will it not hinder it, but it can also benefit it. I think everyone will agree. When the US silver policy changes, or when other factors occur that can help China get out of its current difficulties, this dual currency can be abolished immediately.

Finally, I feel that for the purpose I said, it seems less difficult to find a British pound loan than any reason previously put forward to the UK, which has been met with difficulties. (End)

Soong Tzu-wen Expresses Disapproval of the Sassoon Plan: Issuing Pound Notes is No Different From Adding Another Currency System, Which Will Cause Financial Disorder in Our Country 109

Central News Agency reports that Soong Tzu-wen, a standing committee member of the National Economic Committee, met with the giants of the local banking industry, Ye Zhuotang, Tang Shoumin, Li Fuxun, Xi Demao, and the Director of the Coinage Department of the Ministry of Finance, Xu Kan, at his residence yesterday morning to discuss opinions on stabilizing the local financial situation, and discuss the relief plan for Shanghai's financial situation published by Sir Sassoon. Mr. Soong then met with reporters from various newspapers at his residence at 12:00 p.m. and expressed his opinions as follows:

Dare Not Agree With Sassoon's Opinion

According to Mr. Soong, Sir Sassoon's financial relief plan advocates issuing Shanghai pound notes to relieve the financial panic in this city. I believe that if this move is realized, it will be enough to make the financial situation in our country more disordered. Because our country already has a currency system that circulates in the market, if Shanghai pound notes are issued again, it is no different from adding another currency system to our country, and the financial disorder will inevitably become more serious. Therefore, I dare not express my approval of Sassoon's suggestion. I predict that the financial authorities will definitely not approve of this either. The current instability of our country's financial situation is due to the instability of people's hearts. Therefore, if we want to seek financial stability, we must first stabilize people's hearts. As for the matter of local real estate merchant Cheng Linsheng and others initiating the raising of 450 million yuan in real estate circulating notes, Mr. Soong believes that it has not yet been studied whether this move can be enough to relieve the market.

Three Banks Cooperate, Financial Solidarity

The government has always intended to promote thorough cooperation between the three banks, the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, so that our country's financial solidarity and capital can be increased to cope with difficult times. This time, the National Government appointed Zhang Gongquan as the vice president of the Central Bank in order to develop the bank's future business. After the Bank of China increases its government shares, the government will send me to be a director of the bank's government shares, because there is an explicit provision in the articles of association for the government to send directors. As for the original system of the Bank of China, it is unlikely to change much. The chairman of the board must be selected from among the directors, so the statement that I have been appointed is quite inconsistent. The statement of concurrently serving as general manager has never been heard. After the Bank of Communications increases its government shares, it will also add several directors, which has not yet been determined.

Full Standing Committee Meeting Will Be Held Next Month

Mr. Soong continued, the 12th Standing Committee Meeting of the National Economic Committee will be held in Nanjing next month. I am currently preparing proposals for discussion and implementation. At that time, I will go to Nanjing and fly directly to Sichuan from Nanjing, but the exact date has not yet been decided.

Customs Explanation Supplement: Measures to Encourage the Import of Foreign Silver, So That All Merchants May Understand Clearly and Avoid Misunderstandings 111

Tang Haian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Tax Commissioner Luford, in order to explain and supplement the regulations for the duty-free re-export of imported foreign silver, issued Joint Announcement No. 1440 yesterday, stating: "Regarding the regulations for the duty on import of foreign silver and subsequent re-export, this Customs has already issued Announcement No. 1431. Now, we have received an order from the Ministry of Finance to explain the first item of the aforementioned regulations and supplement the second item. We are to comply and announce this to the public, etc." In accordance with this, the full text of the regulations as currently explained and supplemented is transcribed below: (1) Foreign imported raw silver or national currency (each national currency should be based on containing 23.493448 grams of pure silver) will be allowed to be registered with the importing Customs with the imported amount and date. The Customs will issue a certificate. In the future, if there is a need for re-export, the original importer may submit the original certificate to the Ministry to exchange for a duty-free passport for the original amount of raw silver or national currency for export. The so-called "original amount" refers to the fact that when re-exporting, the raw silver and national currency of the same quantity as the original import shall be allowed, and it is not limited to the originally imported raw silver and national currency. If it is re-exported in batches, this passport may also be used, but it is limited to the amount listed on the original passport. (2) Those who hold the aforementioned duty-free passport for export, in addition to paying a tax of 2.25% (national currency and bars from the Central Mint are exempt from the 2.25% tax), the silver export tax and equalization tax levied from October 15th of the 23rd year will be exempted from full payment. (3) The import of raw silver must not be less than 500,000 ounces per time. If it is national currency, it should be converted and calculated. Let all merchants be aware of this. This announcement is hereby made.

Yesterday, the Jianghai Customs issued an announcement regarding the order from the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance to transfer the Xinyang Port sub-station, which belonged to the Jiaohai Customs, to the direct jurisdiction of the Jianghai Customs. Let all merchants be aware of this. This announcement is hereby made. March 27th, 24th year of the Republic of China, Superintendent Tang Haian, Tax Commissioner Luford.

Spring Relief News from the Chinese and Foreign Charity Association 115

The Chinese and Foreign Charity Association at 97 Renji Road believes that last year's drought was severe, and the disaster relief in various counties of Jiangsu and Ningbo is still ongoing, while the spring famine has arrived. In addition to Yixing and Liyang, which have jointly appointed special relief commissioners with the Jisheng Association to proceed in an orderly manner, the disaster in Haining, Zhejiang, is particularly severe. Last winter, it jointly implemented emergency relief with the Jisheng Association. Now, the wheat season is still far away, and there is a shortage of food. The disaster victims are all waiting to die. However, the association's funds have been exhausted. At this time, Zhu Xiangsheng and Songsheng, brothers and owners of the Yuanhe Shendou Maixing in the South City, who are happy to do good deeds, generously donated 400 bags of white rice, designating the villages of Xieqiao and Qingyun in that county for relief. In addition, Mr. Chen Zhinai donated 35 bags of rice, designating the Yanguan Town in the urban area, and entrusted the association to choose the most needy areas for distribution. This can be described as timely relief. The association sent personnel and invited Father Ding Maoliang of the Chang'an Catholic Church, along with Cui Jialu, Ye Duomao, Fang Shaoyao, and Liu Baokang, to assist in the actual investigation and distribution. Mr. Yang Zhongyao also provided voluntary assistance. The investigation and distribution was completed the day before yesterday. According to the report returned to Shanghai, the drought last year was very severe, and there was no harvest. In addition, in the past three years, the silkworm industry has suffered a tragic decline, and the rural economy has gone bankrupt. Most of the strong men have fled due to the famine. The elderly, weak, and women are begging for food in the towns and cities, all eating thin porridge with bran and wild vegetables. Their faces are pale. They even disregard the wind and rain, dismantling houses and selling bricks to seek a full meal. In this situation, they are unable to cultivate in the spring, which will have a significant impact on the future. The relief workers believe that the disaster victims are eagerly awaiting food, so they should urgently investigate and distribute it. This time, 4,000 households received relief. With three people per household, it can still save tens of thousands of people from immediate crisis. However, it is also a drop in the bucket. We urgently hope that all sectors will continue to maintain this effort to avoid losing all previous efforts.

Cheng Yiqing Discusses the Tragic Disaster in Jiangdu and Calls for Urgent Relief 116

The disaster areas in more than ten counties in Jiangsu Province, such as Liyang, Lishui, and Gaochun, have been allocated funds and personnel by the Drought Relief Association and various charitable organizations for relief. Although it is a drop in the bucket, providing assistance in times of need can still save many lives. The northwestern and southern villages (i.e., Zones 8 and 9) of Jiangdu have also suffered a severe disaster. Despite repeated appeals, no relief has been provided. According to Mr. Cheng Yiqing, who has returned to Shanghai after inspection, the northwestern and southern villages of the county are vast, almost equal to the area of another small county. The disaster-affected area is estimated to be hundreds of square miles, with more than 100,000 disaster-stricken households. The disaster is due to years of drought and famine, which was particularly severe last year, resulting in almost no harvest. The disaster victims have been without grain for a long time. Fortunately, the winter was not cold, and they were able to survive on green vegetables, radishes, and yams. Now, the grass roots have been eaten almost entirely. The disaster victims' faces are withered, their waists are bent, and they are desperately waiting for help.

Round-the-World Giant Liner "Empress of Britain" Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday; Many of the More Than 500 Passengers Are Wealthy and Distinguished; After Touring the City, It Departed for Qinhuangdao Last Night 123

The giant liner "Empress of Britain," owned by the Changxing Company, which cruises around the world, arrived in Shanghai at 7:30 yesterday morning with 516 tourists. The passengers are all wealthy Europeans and Americans, including a Prussian princess. After arriving in Shanghai, the passengers visited the South City and Zhabei. After having lunch at 華 懋, they left Shanghai that night and headed for Qinhuangdao. Details are as follows:

Arrived in Shanghai in the Morning: The ship is the company's largest, with a registered tonnage of 42,500 tons, a length of 755 feet, and a width of 97.5 feet. It departed from New York on January 10th, crossed the Atlantic Ocean, and arrived via the Suez Canal. It arrived in Hong Kong on the 23rd of this month, stayed in port for four days, and set sail on the 27th, arriving in Shanghai at 7:30 yesterday morning. The ship berthed outside Wusongkou. The Changxing Company of this city dispatched one or two small steamers in two batches from 4:30 in the morning to welcome the passengers. The first batch landed at the new customs pier at 9:45, and the second batch landed at the new customs pier at 10:30.

Visiting the City in Batches: After the more than 500 passengers landed in two batches, they took cars to visit the South City and Zhabei. The first batch went to the Fanwangdu Garden in the South City and then to Zhabei before returning to the Cathay Hotel to rest. The second batch went to Zhabei first and then to the South City, also returning to the Cathay Hotel to rest and have lunch. After the visit, they returned to the Empress of Britain in Wusong.

Distinguished Guests on Board: In addition to Professor and Mrs. Skray of Yale University, Commander Sir William Walton and the Finnish Consul General Xinbaoge, Princess Joachim of Prussia also came on the same ship. The princess is visiting China for the first time and boarded the second batch of small steamers at 10:30. In addition, the company's branch manager, Parker, accompanied the group to Beiping. He will return to Shanghai in ten days. Also, Steele, the chief of traffic of the Beining Railway, took the ship to China, went to Beiping, and returned to his original position.

Departed North Last Night: After lunch, the passengers went out at will to shop for miscellaneous items. At about 8 o'clock, they returned to the Cathay Hotel to hold a tea dance party. At 10:30, they returned to the original ship Empress of Britain and set sail from Wusong at about 12:00 that night, heading north to Qinhuangdao. It is scheduled to arrive on the 31st of this month, transfer to a special train of the Beining Railway to Beiping for sightseeing. It is scheduled to stay in Beiping for four days, and then leave Qinhuangdao for Beppu, Japan, on the 5th of next month, then via Kobe and Yokohama, return to the United States via Honolulu, and is scheduled to return to New York on May 20th.

The City Was Sunny and Cold Yesterday; China Aviation Planes Have Taken Off Successively; It Turned Cloudy Again from 1:00 PM 124

After the wind subsided slightly the day before yesterday afternoon, the weather in this city was sunny yesterday morning. The Shanghai-Beiping, Shanghai-Hankou, and Shanghai-Guangdong planes, which were stranded in Shanghai by the wind and rain the day before yesterday, took off successively in the morning. However, at about 1:00 PM, dark clouds suddenly rose slowly and covered the sun, and the sky turned cloudy again. It did not clear up until evening, and the weather remained sunny and cold all day long, still like winter.

Anti-Spitting Campaign 125

Workers' Day: Since the China Anti-Tuberculosis Association launched the anti-spitting campaign, in order to promote it universally and achieve practical results, it has specially stipulated Students' Day, Workers' Day, Merchants' Day, and various organizations' days. The conference opened at the Lido Grand Theater the day before yesterday. All sectors are assisting in the implementation with all their efforts. Yesterday was the second day of the campaign, Workers' Day. The Shanghai General Trade Union supervised all trade unions and workers to mobilize and promote it widely. In addition to printing and distributing a letter to workers, they also sent people to major factories to persuade and warn workers. At the same time, the trade unions held separate meetings to lecture on the harm of spitting and methods of preventing tuberculosis, so that all workers could be vigilant. After listening to the lectures, the workers also promoted it to their families and friends.

Merchants' Day: Today is Merchants' Day. The city's Chamber of Commerce has instructed all businesses to post slogans and declarations inside the counters to promote it. At the same time, large slogans spanning the roads, such as "No Spitting on Roads, Cars, and Public Places," were posted on Nanjing Road, Gongguan Road, and North Railway Station to attract the attention of citizens. The City Chamber of Commerce issued a declaration yesterday, which stated: "The most important things are often started from the most subtle and superficial things. Spitting anywhere is regarded as a very common and unimportant thing by most people. However, once germs are spread, it can lead to loss of life in serious cases and medical expenses in minor cases, causing loss of money or even loss of employment due to illness. Not to mention the health of the entire nation, personal loss is already not small. So, why do people spit anywhere? It is just for laziness and convenience. No matter how tight one's economy is, it is always possible to prepare a spittoon at home or in the store. When a person goes out, a handkerchief is always carried. Therefore, it is not difficult to avoid spitting anywhere. As long as you get rid of the laziness and convenience, you may feel a little unaccustomed at first, but it will become natural over time. Therefore, the Chamber of Commerce will add a few words to the meaning of the Anti-Spitting Campaign Conference, hoping that all business circles in the city will pay attention."
