According to the "North China Daily News," the British China General Omnibus Company held its 12th annual shareholders' meeting at Sassoon House on Thursday (28th) at 4:00 PM. Silver Dollars with Hollowed Centers Filled with Lead; Convicts Sentenced After Appeal 127

On the afternoon of January 14th of this year, the French police cracked down on an organization that manufactured counterfeit silver dollars at No. 3, Lane 372, East End, Dapu Bridge, Xujiahui Road. The center of the new version of silver dollars made by the Central Mint in the 23rd year was hollowed out and filled with lead to be used and mixed in the market. The principal offender, Lin Tai from Fujian, and six accomplices, Chen Chuncheng, Mei Yunguong, Huang Puwen, Lin Jianan, and Wei Shun from Fuzhou and Wenzhou, were arrested on the spot. Equipment, lathes, wind furnaces, lead bars, and more than 100 empty silver dollar shells and a basin of silver skin were seized. They were sent to the Second Special Court for prosecution. After the trial, Lin Tai, Wei Shun, Chen Chuncheng, and Huang Puwen were each sentenced to five years of imprisonment and five years of deprivation of civil rights. Mei Yunguong and Lin Jianan were each sentenced to three years of imprisonment and three years of deprivation of civil rights. All the exhibits were confiscated. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. However, the convicts were dissatisfied with the original sentence and appealed to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court. The collegial panel of the Higher Court conducted a retrial. After the debate, the date for the sentence was set for the day before yesterday. Chief Judge Guo, along with Two judges, and Prosecutor Zhang opened the court and ordered the appellants to be brought to court. The sentence was revoked, and the six people, including Lin Tai, were each reduced to two years and six months of imprisonment. After the sentencing, the appellants were returned to the detention center to await the final sentence before being sent to prison.

Dentist Zhang Weiliang Accused of Assaulting His Wife; Isn't Once Enough? Past Love Flows Away 128

The Brothers Dental Hospital at No. 3 Zhifu Road was founded by the dentist Zhang Weiliang and his brothers. Weiliang is the youngest. Since its opening, the business has been doing well. Ten years ago, a female student surnamed Dong from Ningbo, who was studying at the Patriotic Girls' School, sought treatment from Zhang Weiliang for a dental disease. They became acquainted. At that time, Zhang was just a young man in his early twenties and had no partner. He found Ms. Dong to be beautiful and well-educated, so he was very fond of her. He tried hard to pursue her, and soon the lovers became a couple. They rented a house at No. 1057 Siwen Lane, Xinzha Road, and lived together. For ten years, they loved each other and had a harmonious relationship. However, in recent years, Zhang's wife, Ms. Dong, suspected that her husband was ambitious and did not return home at night, and that living expenses were often lacking. She advised Weiliang, which angered him, and quarrels often occurred. One day, the couple had a dispute over a minor matter, which turned into violence. Ms. Zhang Dong was injured in the assault and reported it to the police station. Zhang Weiliang was summoned to the First Special Court for a trial. The court advised Ms. Zhang Dong not to hurt the past feelings over such a trivial matter between husband and wife, which is a common occurrence. Ms. Zhang heard the advice and expressed her agreement. The case was withdrawn. However, not long after, at about 2:00 PM on the 18th of last month, Ms. Zhang Dong went to the Brothers Dental Hospital to question her husband because he had reverted to his old ways and was not providing enough living expenses. They disagreed and eventually resorted to violence. At this time, Ms. Zhang Dong was six months pregnant and nearing her due date. After being assaulted, she was in pain all over her body. Out of resentment, she reported to the Laozha Police Station. Detective Sun Dafa was sent to investigate and sent her to the hospital to verify the injuries. He reported back to the police chief, who requested the First Special Court to issue a summons. Last Thursday, Zhang Weiliang was summoned to the Second Criminal Court. Police lawyer Zhang Shizhu prosecuted him for injury under Article 293 of the Criminal Law. After the interrogation, the hearing was adjourned to another date. Yesterday morning, the case was scheduled for a further hearing, but Ms. Zhang Dong had given birth a week ago and was unable to attend. Judge Zhan Liangce briefly questioned the defendant Zhang Weiliang and ordered Zhang to provide a guarantor who would be available at any time and adjourned the hearing to the morning of the 24th.

Fast-Moving Truck Runs Over Female Teacher; Two Rickshaw Pullers Also Seriously Injured 129

Sang Zhichen, a woman from Ningbo, 22 years old, is currently working as a teacher at the Ningbo Seventh Elementary School in Jinchun Lane, Meibai Road. Yesterday morning at 11:00, she hired a rickshaw No. 8301 from the North Station to go to school. The rickshaw puller's name was Dong Gaowen (33 years old, from Yancheng, living at No. 11 Changxing Lane, Eryang Road, Zhabei). When the rickshaw drove to the entrance of the Xinzha car shop on Avenue Edward VII, a truck suddenly drove up from behind, registered as No. 16525. Because the driver was driving at full speed and could not stop, it slammed into Sang's rickshaw, causing the young woman Sang Zhichen to be run over by the truck's wheels and severely injured. She lost consciousness on the spot. The rickshaw puller Dong Gaowen also suffered a head injury and was bleeding. At that time, another rickshaw puller named Zhu Xinghe, 41 years old, from Jiangbei (living at a certain number, Nanlin Lane, Hengfeng Road, Zhabei) was also pulling an empty rickshaw coming from the opposite direction, and was caught in the crossfire. His leg bone was crushed, and blood flowed like a torrent. The Xinzha Police Station saw this and quickly recorded the number of the car that caused the accident. The truck driver was detained in the police station for investigation. The three injured were sent to Baolong Hospital for treatment. It is said that Sang's internal injuries are so severe that her life may be in danger.

Chen Fengshi, a veteran revolutionary comrade, embraced the doctrine early in his life and worked for the revolution. In the 7th year of the Republic, he served as the General Staff Officer under Xiong Kewu's command, fighting to the death with the warlords of the Northern Army. In the 9th year of the Republic, he resigned from his military post and subsequently served as a counselor of the Grand Marshal's Office. In recent years, he lived at home due to heart disease. Procedures for Applying for Private Rickshaw Licenses 132

The Public Concession Work Bureau issued Proclamation No. 4571 yesterday regarding the newly revised procedures for applying for private rickshaw licenses, which reads: "Proclamation. It has been noted that private rickshaw licenses will no longer be issued by the Donation and Tax Section of this Bureau's General Office after 5:00 PM on March 28th of this year. In the future, applications must be made at the Private Rickshaw Licensing Office at 596 Gongping Road during the following hours: From October 1st to the end of April, from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM; from May 1st to the end of September, from 8:30 AM to 12:00 PM and from 2:00 PM to 3:30 PM. The licensing hours on Saturdays will be until 11:30 AM. The following newly revised procedures will be implemented from March 29th of this year. All those who wish to apply for private rickshaw licenses for the quarter beginning April 1st of this year are requested to take note of the following: The application form must be signed or stamped by the license holder. Blank application forms can be obtained from the Private Rickshaw Licensing Office on Gongping Road, the Donation and Tax Section of this Bureau's General Office, and various police stations. Each applicant should fill out the application form as required and submit it to the Licensing Office on Gongping Road, where a license number will be assigned. In the future, the original license holder should continue to use this number when renewing the license each quarter. The porcelain license plate issued by this Bureau should be affixed to the upper left side of the rickshaw. When paying the license fee, the small porcelain tag, which indicates the license number and has a different color each quarter, should be attached to the license plate to easily identify whether the license has expired. Registered license holders are responsible for paying the license fee as long as they retain the license plate. If they do not wish to renew the license, they should return the license plate to the Licensing Office. If the license holder does not renew the license within twenty-one days after the license expires, this Bureau may consider the license to be canceled and reassign the number to someone else. A registration fee of five jiao in silver currency should be paid when the license number is assigned. Therefore, those who wish to apply for the June quarter license should pay their representative eight yuan and five jiao in silver currency if they do not collect it in person. When renewing the license each quarter, eight yuan will be charged as usual. Residents of the French Concession and the Nanshi area should apply to the French Concession Public Works Bureau for licenses valid for both concessions. Residents of the Public Concession and the roads outside the concession, or Zhabei, should apply to this Bureau for licenses valid for both concessions. If a business or other organization wishes to apply for licenses for vehicles used by its employees, they should apply to this Bureau or the French Concession Public Works Bureau, depending on where the headquarters or main office is located. When filling out the application form, be careful to ensure that all information provided is accurate. If a license is obtained by falsifying names or addresses, it will be revoked upon discovery. This proclamation is hereby issued for general knowledge."

Special District Rickshaw Guild – Preventing Lessors from Overcharging Rental Fees – Vehicle Committee Orders Owners to Introduce Rickshaw Pullers for Registration – Misunderstanding Arises in the French Concession from Investigation of Owners and Pullers 133

The Public Concession Work Bureau's Rickshaw Affairs Committee will continue to order rickshaw owners to introduce rickshaw pullers for registration. The Special District Rickshaw Guild has issued a notice to prevent lessors from overcharging rental fees. A misunderstanding has arisen in the French Concession from the investigation of owners and pullers by the police. The details are as follows:

Vehicle Committee Orders Recommendation of Pullers

The Public Concession Work Bureau's Rickshaw Affairs Committee has decided to issue 9,990 rickshaw puller recommendation forms in early April, when the April rickshaw licenses are issued, to facilitate rickshaw owners in continuing the procedure of recommending and completing the registration of rickshaw pullers. In addition, each rickshaw owner will be issued an investigation form, requesting them to fill in the names and addresses of those who lease their vehicles, in order to facilitate investigation.

Guild Prevents Overcharging of Rental Fees

The Special District Office of the Rickshaw Guild issued a notice to all rickshaw owners yesterday to prevent the overcharging of rental fees, which reads: "Notice. It has been found that on August 6th of the 23rd year of the Republic of China, the representatives of this office and the representatives of the Public Concession Bureau agreed that the rental fee should be 7 jiao 8 fen in silver dollars per vehicle per day, plus 7 fen in silver dollars for the mutual aid fund, for a total of 8 jiao 5 fen. Furthermore, on November 23rd, the Public Concession Bureau's Rickshaw Affairs Committee and the representatives of this office exchanged documents approving the collection of additional fees for savings, accommodation, and other expenses, but receipts must be issued and accounted for. This is a mutually agreed-upon decision and cannot be changed without the consent of both parties. According to an investigation by the Public Concession Bureau's Rickshaw Affairs Committee, some lessors are reportedly overcharging rental fees, which violates the agreement between this office and the Public Concession Bureau. Although the lessors are responsible for the losses suffered by the rickshaw owners, the rickshaw owners are still responsible under the license regulations. All members are requested to check the rental collection methods of the lessors at any time and ensure that they strictly comply with the regulations agreed upon between this office and the Public Concession Bureau. Otherwise, rickshaw owners shall be responsible for any disputes that may arise. This notice is hereby issued."

Misunderstanding Arises from Investigation of Owners

The French Concession police are investigating rickshaw owners in the southern Shanghai area, and some rickshaw pullers mistakenly believe that the French Concession will follow the British Concession in registering rickshaw pullers, including taking photographs and fingerprints. Therefore, they have returned to their hometowns in droves. The Rickshaw Guild has issued a notice to all rickshaw owners to explain the situation, which reads: "Recently, the French Concession police have sent personnel to investigate the real rickshaw owners in the Nanshi area. Their intention is to facilitate future management. However, this has led to some rickshaw pullers spreading all kinds of unfounded rumors and rushing back to their villages as if a great disaster were about to befall them. Their desperate situation is also pitiful. According to reports from various rickshaw businesses, this self-inflicted disturbance is affecting the livelihoods of the poor and social order. Therefore, we earnestly advise all rickshaw businesses to guide their rickshaw pullers to work with peace of mind and not to be misled by these rumors, which will harm themselves and others. If you see any unscrupulous elements spreading rumors, you can take them to the nearest police station for interrogation to eliminate these harmful elements and serve as a warning to others. Please pay attention and do not listen to rumors."

Shanghai Bank Robbery Appeal 134

On the morning of November 21st of last year, the Shanghai Bank's Yuyuan Road branch in western Shanghai sent a clerk with 5,200 yuan in cash in a bank-owned car to the Xujiahui Jiaotong University Savings Office. On the way, in the French Concession on Haig Road, peasants carrying straw blocked the road. Suddenly, robbers rushed forward and stole all the money before escaping. Afterwards, the French police special unit arrested the robbers Zhang Zilong, Huang Shuncai, Fei A'mei, Huang Yaosheng, Zhu Xuenneng (the messenger from Jiaotong University), and more than ten others. Over 200 yuan in stolen money was recovered. It was also found that Zhang Zilong had previously committed two other robberies in the French Concession. They were sent to the Second Special District Court, and the police lawyer filed a public prosecution for gang robbery. After the trial, Zhang Zilong was sentenced to three counts of robbery, serving eleven years of imprisonment. Huang Shuncai was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment. Fei A'mei, Huang Yaosheng, and Zhu Xuenneng were each sentenced to five years of imprisonment. The remaining defendants were either not prosecuted due to the police finding no evidence of a crime, or acquitted because there was no evidence of a crime. These details have been reported previously. Now, the five robbers Zhang, Huang, Fei, and Zhu have appealed to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. The High Court, according to the appeal, specially opened an investigation court yesterday, presided over by Judge Fan Pei'en. Each defendant stated their reasons for appeal, either complaining that the sentence was too heavy or denying the crime. They were vague about the real reasons. After verifying the statements, the court ordered a postponement for further investigation and interrogation. The appellants were returned to the detention center.

Yueyang Maru Collides with Coal Boat – Barge Industry Guild is Negotiating 136

The No. 1390 barge of the Xin Quanji Barge Company, loaded with 47 tons of Beipiao coal dust from Shihe Coal Company, was passing by the Dachu Warehouse at 1:30 PM on March 28th when the Japanese ship Yueyang Maru was entering the port and intending to dock. The black ball was not raised, nor was a sound made. Due to the shipowner's careless steering, the ship blocked the river with its bow facing east and its stern facing west. As a result, the blades of the ship's stern struck the coal boat amidships, causing the boat and its cargo to sink completely. All the workers fell into the water at the same time. Fortunately, they were rescued by a boat and did not drown. The losses were enormous. The barge company has reported the incident to the Shanghai Coal and Stone Barge Industry Guild, which has forwarded it to the River and Sea Customs Ship Management Office for a fair judgment. In the meantime, the Guild is directly negotiating with the Nissin Steamship Company.

Municipal Council Approves Telephone Price Increase – Taxpayers Association Sends Stern Letter of Inquiry Yesterday – Requests Special Attention to Two Points 137

Since the Public Concession Municipal Council agreed to a 12.5% price increase requested by the Telephone Company, public opinion has been in an uproar. The Chinese Taxpayers Association, believing that the Municipal Council has disregarded the opinions of taxpayers, sent a stern letter of inquiry yesterday, which reads: "Sir, the case of the Shanghai Telephone Company's request for a price increase has been under observation by this Association, and we requested your council to postpone the review, but we have not yet received a reply. According to reports, the head of your council's finance department believes that only a 12.5% increase should be allowed. Whether this calculation is reasonable is not our concern. However, the fact that your council has not paid attention to the opinions of taxpayers has been demonstrated by the facts and cannot be ignored by taxpayers. The opposition to the telephone price increase has been overwhelming in the city recently, and those who have come to this Association to express their opposition, such as general users on Nanjing Road, are even more agitated. From the perspective of this Association: (1) The commercial situation is so precarious, and capital profits are declining. Forcing the Telephone Company to obtain a 10% profit is unfair. (2) Forcing the Telephone Company to obtain a 10% profit, thereby increasing the burden on taxpayers and reducing their tax-paying ability, is benefiting a private business at the expense of public revenue. (3) Metering by call, according to tests, a single phone is about one to ten, and several phones are at least one to three. That is, beyond the monthly limit of one hundred calls, according to the former example, one would actually need a thousand calls, and according to the latter example, one would actually need three hundred calls. In this case, although the usage fee is nominally ten yuan per month, according to the former example, one would actually pay much more than the current rate. After this Association firmly presents the above opinions to your Chairman, we request that special attention be paid to the following two points: (1) Are the interests of taxpayers the same as the interests of the Telephone Company? (2) Where is the foundation of the Municipal Council built? We respectfully request that you investigate and consider the general economic situation and postpone the review of this case. We hope you will do so."

Zhou Guiqing Commits Suicide in a Hotel 140

Zhou Guiqing, a 52-year-old man from Zhejiang, recently came to Shanghai to visit friends and seek employment. On the afternoon of the 27th, at 4:00 PM, he checked into Room 27 of the World Hotel at 9 Huage Road in the French Concession. After checking in, he went out and returned to the hotel at 8:00 PM to sleep. He did not get up until noon the next day. The bellboy knocked on the door and asked if he wanted to extend his stay. After calling for a long time, there was no response. He pried open the door and found Zhou dead in bed, with saliva coming from his mouth. He reported it to the French police, who sent detectives to investigate. No evidence of suicide was found. The body was sent to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall for an autopsy. Several notes with Shanghai addresses were found on the deceased's person. When the addresses were investigated, no one recognized the deceased. Therefore, it was impossible to find and notify his family. Yesterday was a holiday for memorial purposes. The court will request the Second Special District Court to send someone to examine the body today to determine the cause of death.

Old Woman Sentenced for Performing Abortion 141

Zhang Boyong, a worker at the Guangming Glass Factory from Suzhou, lived with Lu Fangshi, a widow, after having an affair with her at 15 North Fujian Road. Recently, Lu Fangshi became pregnant and, fearing that her belly would gradually swell and affect her appearance, she hired midwife Ma Pan to perform an abortion on the 10th of this month. As a result, although the fetus was aborted, Lu Fangshi suffered internal injuries and died after several days despite medical treatment. After the Huisi police learned of this, they arrested Lu Fangshi and Zhang Boyong and sent them to the First Special District Court. The police prosecuted them for abortion under Articles 305 and 307 of the Criminal Code. After several interrogations, the trial has now concluded. Yesterday morning, Judge Liu Yugui, presiding over the Eighth Criminal Court, announced the verdict: Ma Pan, with the intent to profit, received the request of a pregnant woman to perform an abortion, resulting in her death, and was sentenced to two years of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment was finalized will be deducted from the sentence at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Considering her old age, the sentence is suspended for three years. Zhang Boyong was found not guilty. The medicines seized in the case could not be proven to have been used for the crime and should be returned. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin also declared in court that he would waive the appeal. Therefore, both defendants were immediately released.

It is certain that a large number of men and women from all directions will go to see them.

Car Plunges into River 143

A Russian named Skikoff (transliteration), accompanied by his girlfriend, was driving his own car, license number 6577, from west to east on Qiaodun Road near the intersection of Haig Road in western Shanghai at around 9:00 AM yesterday. Due to the high speed, he was unable to brake in time, and the car plunged into the river. The front glass was shattered, and Skikoff and his girlfriend were seriously injured. Two Attempted Suicides by Drowning, Both Rescued 144

Yesterday, two attempted suicides by drowning occurred on the Dongchang Road ferry in Pudong. The sailors on the ferry rescued the victims and handed them over to the police, who took them to the Pudong Branch Bureau. Because they were both suffering from economic hardship, they were transferred to the General Bureau for relief.

Xu Xiaofa: stated that he was 24 years old and from Ningbo. His home is in the pavilion room above the rice store next to Shen Shunjie Laundry on Fuli Road in the French Concession. His brother-in-law, Tang Ruishun, works at the store. He attempted suicide because he was suffering from economic hardship. A suicide note was found on his person, which reads: "I have been unemployed for several months and am suffering from economic hardship. I have no choice but to take this course of action. I hope that a kind gentleman will grant me a coffin. Your boundless merit will be repaid in the next life. I will not go into detail. Sacrificed person, Xu Xiaofa."

Jin Long: stated that he was 19 years old and from Changzhou. He lived within the small passenger line in the French Concession. He brought 200 yuan from his hometown to Shanghai to buy goods, but it was stolen by a thief at the station. He has been relying on pawning his clothes to survive and cannot return home. A wallet was found on his person containing eight pawn tickets, which were pawned within the last ten days, with pawn values ranging from three jiao to four yuan. This is also a pathetic situation.

(4) Agriculture This year, China's rural economy has been affected by the global recession and domestic banditry and famine, and the problems are becoming more serious. In terms of famine, the provinces affected by drought include Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Henan, Hebei, Gansu, Guizhou, and Shanxi, a total of eleven provinces, with 635 counties affected. The affected area totaled 32.9 million mu, accounting for 47% of the cultivated land area of the eleven provinces. Although the floods were relatively mild, the affected provinces and regions also reached fourteen, including Hubei, Hunan, Hebei, Henan, Shanxi, Sichuan, Anhui, Shaanxi, Jiangxi, Fujian, Min, Chahar, Shandong, Guizhou, a total of 283 counties, with an affected area of about 30 million mu. And the damage caused by wind and insects is not included. The losses caused by agricultural disasters, only the drought item, in terms of quantity, includes 21.6 million shi of rice, 31.2 million shi of sorghum, 25 million shi of corn, 40 million shi of millet, 6 million shi of cotton, and 31.6 million shi of soybeans. The loss of rice is the largest in Jiangsu, totaling 41 million shi, while the percentage is the highest in Anhui, only 62% of the usual year's harvest. Hebei Province suffered the most losses of sorghum, corn, and millet, and Jiangsu Province also suffered the largest losses of cotton and soybeans. In terms of grid value, rice is worth 68.4 million yuan, sorghum is worth 7.2 million yuan, corn is worth 6.7 million yuan, soybeans are worth 12.9 million yuan, cotton is worth 19.9 million yuan, and millet is worth 51.7 million yuan, totaling more than 170 million yuan. Including other famine losses, the total should exceed 180 million yuan.

In terms of production volume, according to the fourth estimate of the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute, the average total harvest of winter crops in various provinces is about 70% of a full year. The provinces in Central and Southern China are better than those in Northern China. In terms of product type, wheat in the main producing areas of Northern China was a poor harvest. Hebei Province only reached 50% of a full year, Shandong Province only reached 66%, and Henan Province only reached 59%. The harvest volume of other crops such as barley, peas, broad beans, and rapeseed was similar to wheat in these three regions. The average harvest volume of summer crops in various provinces was less than 60% of a full year, about 70% of a normal year. Among them, Fujian, Guangdong, Guangxi, Yunnan, etc., were better, reaching more than 70% of a full year. Shandong, Hebei, Shanxi, etc., were next, reaching about 70% of a full year. Jiangsu, Henan, Shaanxi, Gansu, Qinghai, Ningxia, Suiyuan, Chahar, Sichuan, and Guizhou, etc., were next again, reaching about 60% of a full year. Other provinces such as Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, and Hunan had the lowest, only 40% to 50% of a full year. In terms of product type, rice and soybeans accounted for about 55% of a full year, glutinous rice accounted for 57%, cotton accounted for 56%, sorghum and sweet potatoes accounted for 63%, millet accounted for 64%, corn and sesame accounted for 59%, peanuts accounted for 62%, and tobacco and broomcorn millet accounted for 61%. China's agricultural production technology has been very degraded, coupled with the rampant disasters, and it is difficult to expect a bumper harvest.

In terms of agricultural product prices, prices fell sharply in the first five months. For example, the average price of Suzhou Tong glutinous rice in April was only 6 yuan and 80 cents per shi, a decrease of more than 30 cents compared to the same period last year. The average price of railway wheat in May was 6 yuan and 30 cents per hectoliter, a decrease of 1 yuan and 40 cents compared to the same period last year. The average price of Shanghai cotton in April was 42 yuan, 65 cents, a decrease of 5 yuan, 37 cents compared to the same period last year. After June, affected by the drought, rice and wheat prices rose. Cotton prices also tended to rise due to the later listing of Henan and Shaanxi cotton and the strong purchases by foreign merchants. The average price of Suzhou Tong glutinous rice in August rose to 11 yuan and 70 cents. The price of railway wheat in December rose to 8 yuan. The average price of Shanghai cotton in August also rose to more than 7 yuan and 80 cents. For the general trend of agricultural product prices, please refer to Table 8. According to the table, grains, textile raw materials, beans, and kernels all fell first and then rose, while livestock products all trended downward. The overall index was 5.3% lower than in the 22nd year. (To be continued)

Free Talk

Where Did Alcestis Go? 162

— Hu Luo

Ibsen wrote "A Doll's House," and Nora finally shouted, "I'm leaving immediately." So Nora left the family and went into society. Naturally, Ibsen could only write up to this point. He could never tell us what would happen to Nora when she entered society, and whether the problems would be easily solved after entering society? Ibsen couldn't solve these problems.

Because a certain professor told me that classical works generally have no content. He specifically pointed out Moliere, saying that Moliere's works are also empty of content and have no thought. I was skeptical, so I found a copy of "The Misanthrope" to read. As a result, I discovered that the professor had deceived me. "The Misanthrope" has content. (Originally, content and form are an inseparable unity.) From "The Misanthrope," I saw a male Nora. He is the protagonist of "The Misanthrope," "Alcestis." Alcestis is a misanthrope, he hates the hypocrisy of the world, he hates those aristocrats who wear masks. The aristocrats are so hypocritical, formalistic, and falsely modest. Therefore, Alcestis indignantly said: "A swindler, a shameless rogue, a confounded robber, everyone thinks so, no one denies it. However, his ugliness is welcomed everywhere: everyone entertains him, everyone greets him with a smile, he has a place everywhere; even the most capable people cannot compete with him." Alcestis was distressed. Because he honestly criticized an aristocrat's poem, saying, "Your poem is only good for throwing in the toilet." Therefore, the aristocrat sued him. He also discovered that his lover was so false and lewd; his honesty also provoked others to slander him. So, he was saddened, he extremely hated this world. Finally, he decided to break away from this sinful society and go to the desert. In the last act, he said: "I am deceived everywhere, oppressed by all kinds of injustice. I am going to jump out of this evil-ridden 壑, go far away to find a remote place where I can freely be a gentleman."

Nora and Alcestis are somewhat similar: Nora wants to break away from the hateful doll family, and Alcestis wants to break away from this hateful society. However, neither Ibsen nor Moliere can completely solve the problems of Nora and Alcestis.

In fact, "Alcestis is Moliere himself, representing a bourgeois surrounded by an aristocratic environment and resisting it." Moliere has a kind of great spirit, not at all like the professor thinks he is a writer who flatters the aristocracy. He "violently attacked the aristocracy, he mocked the powerful people of the time with great boldness." When "Tartuffe" was publicly performed, it aroused the anger of the monks, and the priests and archbishops all sued him. When Napoleon I read his work, he said: "If this play were made in my time, then I would not allow it to be performed." Therefore, Moliere is not a flatterer of the aristocracy, but a rebel of the aristocracy. From "The Misanthrope," can't you see how much Moliere hates the aristocracy? However, Moliere, like Ibsen, Tolstoy... all wrote about all the social contradictions and ugliness; however, they could not give this "contradiction" a correct solution. Moliere hated society and the aristocracy, but he also lived in this ugly and dirty atmosphere. This contradiction entangled him, so he created an ideal character—Alcestis. Moliere made Alcestis break away from this society and go to the desert to live his "gentleman's" life in solitude. Naturally, this is Moliere's fantasy, and it is also his way of resolving "contradictions." Ibsen brought Nora out of the family, thinking that he had solved the women's problem; similarly, Moliere made Alcestis break away from society, also thinking that he had solved this ugly social problem.

Today's society is also ugly. Like Alcestis, we also feel contradictions and "melancholy." People are all living hypocritically and uglily. Especially those who live suspended in the air feel a deeper contradiction and hate this society more. However, where does Alcestis ultimately go? As Moliere wrote, to the road of fantasy? However, people can never survive outside of society! Therefore, Alcestis cannot go to the road of fantasy, but should come to reality! Break away from his "court" (old nest) and come into "life"!

Singapore Night 163

— Fei Er

The night of Singapore is seized in the hands of a black devil.

The night, on the seashore of Lion Island, illuminated by electric lights from tall and majestic cement buildings, is the brilliant outer garment of the splendid capitalist land. Inside this garment, however, the night of Singapore is tightly held in the hands of the devil. The heart of the decaying face of the city is turbulent, palpitating, and festering, waiting for the day when the city will be blasted open.

When the clanging sound of money is put away in the vault during the day, the night of Singapore is buried in the excess of money. At dusk, the wealthy use cars to cruise around, and at night, the European and American investors at the Raffles Hotel dance the crazy jazz in the red lights and green wine. The Capital Theater spits out idle rich people who appreciate American-style love dramas; and the streets are crowded with tourists, ice and soda overflowing in the city at night.

In Dapo, the daughters of the empire in the land of the rising sun kneel under the green light to welcome guests, and self-skinned women sell themselves in secret prostitution; in the Great World and the New World, Chinese bosses and young masters are bargaining with women who sell their flesh; this city is full of pitiful women wandering from other countries.

A dark-skinned, rough-looking Indian devil keeps watch for the rich late at night, and a rattan sleeping mat lying in front of a splendid shop looks like a dog kennel. In the corners of quiet streets, dim electric lights illuminate the lonely policeman standing guard. The unemployed once lay on the sidewalks, and the haggard faces illuminated by the dim electric lights looked like ghostly shadows.

Among the crowds enjoying the cool on the hot and bustling Lion Island seashore, the bright night moon will illuminate the wandering, miserable shadows of frustrated people from other countries. Beside the European War Memorial, wandering youths from other countries will gaze north and feel melancholy about their homeland. In the corners of quiet coasts, with a plop, the majestic tide will swallow the life of a weak loser.

When the city falls into the deep night, and silence engulfs the surging tide of humanity, the wealthy will sleep soundly, embracing passionate daughters of the south, while the bodies of the unemployed will be hanging in the suburban groves. Or when the thunder rumbles and the wealthy are awakened from their sweet dreams, one or two gunshots will rob people and steal property. In the morning, the Singapore market will be bustling as usual, while the rulers will rack their brains about the disasters brought about by the "recession."

Even more terrifying are the propaganda articles posted on the pink walls and the leaflets and slogans painted on the electric light poles. The unemployed are making a silent roar in the night of the city, and the colonized people are preparing for a day of turning over. Among the isolated, the witch doctors will actually unite, and among the white people will also emerge "traitors to the country."

Despite the fact that the tall buildings on the Lion Island seashore face the sea with proud postures, and the city lights illuminate the rushing cars, this night in Singapore is nurturing future bombs, wrapping up sins, and burying new pregnancies.

The night in Singapore is the night of a world city. In addition to her individuality, the night in Singapore also has her universal nature of the world.

Night, however, is nurturing the bright tomorrow.

The Wind of February 164

— Zhang Ping

Wrapped in a purple cloth, Fu Sheng felt as if a hazy net had been cast before his eyes, and he dared not take another glance at this ancient home. He lowered his head and walked straight onto the official road.

The sky was high and clear, without a single cloud. The wind of February gently caressed the willow trees beside the official road, but it could not blow away the melancholy that weighed on Fu Sheng's heart.

He couldn't remember when it was, it was almost a dream: in the ancient home he had abandoned, lived an old couple whom Fu Sheng called Father and Mother. In those days, passing a day seemed as easy as scattering grains of sand. Before the sun had even peeked out from the mountain hollow, the fields were already filled with the sound of mountain songs echoing back and forth. His father always watched him go to the fields and greeted him upon his return. The old man was forever smoking his early morning pipe, and he felt that the world had already given mankind more than it deserved. At dinner, he liked to drink a few cups of white liquor, and his wrinkled face would turn as red as the evening glow. Then he would begin to recount the story of how the previous generation started their business, never tiring of the details. But he lacked the talent for storytelling, and the children from the neighborhood who had gathered would automatically disperse. The only listener was Fu Sheng; he didn't feel as satisfied with the story as his father did. He had a hope hidden deep in his heart – a hope to build a business so much bigger than his father's that it would amaze him, built upon his pair of iron arms!

Thinking of this, a surge of heat rose from the bottom of his heart. He wanted to laugh, but he immediately became aware; it was a dream – like a nightmare he woke up from as a child.

He stood still on the bridgehead, his lonely shadow reflected in the river. The people he called Father and Mother had left this world during a succession of hardship-filled days. As his father lay dying, he held Fu Sheng's hand and said, "The world has changed! You must strive!" And with that, he breathed his last.

As that trembling voice rang in his ears, Fu Sheng turned back to stare again at that ancient home and the patch of land overgrown with weeds – his pair of strong arms had already grown sore, and his legs were so tired that they could no longer support his weight; but what was the result of his efforts? A purple cloth bundle on his shoulder!

The February wind gently brushed the hair that hung down to his ears. He looked at the wharf where the boats were docked ahead, and a new hope surged within him, urging him forward.

——At the end of the year, after being released from prison, A'gen enthusiastically invited him to his home, just like when he picked up his purple cloth bundle. A'gen's home had nothing but four collapsing walls and a worthless wooden board.

He gripped Fu Sheng's hand with a force almost like hand-to-hand combat with an enemy. He said, "Our fate is over – the entire Liu Family Village is over! With our pair of strong hands, let's go outside and find a world of gold!"

That voice was like a thunderclap, stunning Fu Sheng. He never knew his pair of hands could be used for anything other than wielding a hoe. He didn't trust A'gen's words. "I will work harder, and this field will bear brilliant fruit again!"

They parted ways at the wharf.

The February wind blew through Liu Family Village, and Fu Sheng's farming tools were completely devoured. There were no more songs in the fields, and the strong men grew fewer and fewer. The entire Liu Family Village was finished!" Only then did he sigh, and pack his belongings into a purple cloth bundle.

As he approached the wharf, the boatman was yawning under the sun. When he saw clearly that it was Fu Sheng, he patted him on the shoulder and said:

"Going to get rich? The wild winds outside are strong, do you know A'gen?"

Looking like a mad dog, the boatman punched Fu Sheng hard on the back:

"Hmph! Joined the bandits! Offering your heads as targets for foreign guns!"

Then he collapsed again:

"My boat, ah!" The boatman cried.

Fu Sheng had lost consciousness. He stood blankly in the February spring wind, listening to the cuckoo's "cuckoo" cry flying overhead.

Street Scene 165

— Zi Gang

In the eastern corner of the Forbidden City, there is a Japanese military camp where strong men often practice shooting or drilling. People who live nearby or pass by often stop and stare as if it were a circus, holding down hearts filled with a bit of terror.

To the east of this military camp is a small alleyway where people of various nationalities live.

Of course, it wouldn't be without its masters – the Chinese. The rest are too numerous to count: Japanese, Americans, British, French...

Foreign company signs are everywhere. Foreign words are painted on the white walls. Some foreign companies have their front doors on the main street and their employee dormitories here. The Japanese mostly hang small wooden plaques with their names on the side of the door, while people of other nationalities mostly nail engraved brass plates on the door.

You won't see towering skyscrapers of dozens of stories. Apart from Chinese-style houses with large gates, there are only small and exquisite two- or three-story foreign-style buildings. Beijing is not like Shanghai, where land is worth its weight in gold.

In these houses, you'll see foreign gentlemen with chests puffed out and bellies protruding, carrying sticks. Their suits are crisp and stiff. Even the Japanese men are all wearing short, stout suits. Only a few Japanese women stroll on the streets in kimonos, and even then, to feel more comfortable and avoid being noticed, they often wear Chinese cheongsams, with only their eyebrows and hairlines revealing their origins. Proud white-skinned women walk in and out of the doorways. Rickshaw pullers gather around, hoping to make a sale. As soon as those feet in pointy high-heeled leather shoes step onto the rickshaw pedal, they dash off. Rickshaw pullers greatly welcome foreign customers, partly because they are greedy for a relatively generous fare (of course, they can't forget the harsh kicks of leather boots), and partly because they are happy to take advantage, muttering a few words under their breath.

"Foreign women are all like they have children, everyone wearing a fur coat inside out!" A self-proclaimed knowledgeable person says:

"Didn't you see the daughters begging in X Hutong!"

However, there doesn't seem to be any poverty in this alley. Instead, in the empty corners of high walls, there are often small, narrow houses that are less than six feet long, with an earthen pit laid horizontally. Moldy clothes and scraps are piled up in the daytime. These are where the Chinese coolies live – even worse than coolies, just some old men with no job and no support. They stare all day long at the foreigners coming and going from their open doorways, feeling as if they never had a youth, and sighing softly. These small mud houses leaning against these foreign buildings and mansions are truly the best contrast.

You're sure to see a rented car or automobile every three minutes. Those riding in the cars are often white people or Japanese people with large families, but the ones pulling the rickshaws and driving the cars are always Chinese. However, the narrow alley has not become a wide alley, and the street with five inches of dirt has not been paved into a smooth asphalt road. When a car approaches you at night, its bright headlights will illuminate the uneven bumps and dents that are hard to see during the day. As the car passes, a layer of dust flies up half a丈 high, drawing dark curses from pedestrians.

The servants of the residents often stand at these doorways, mostly clean and tidy, and able to speak a few words of pidgin English. Neighbors nod from afar, leisurely chatting about trivial matters. Standing in front of them are short-tailed foreign dogs. The foreign dogs don't seem to distinguish nationalities and always obediently listen to the shouts of the yellow-faced servants.

Chinese maids with neatly combed hair and faces also appear at the doorways, holding either blue-eyed, blonde-haired, or children wearing small kimonos. The women speak stiff foreign languages, but the children often adapt and speak short Chinese phrases.

Children aged five or six to seven or eight, regardless of whether they are Chinese or foreign, often play together, building a sandpile or displaying some toys in front of the door. Boundaries disappear among the children. Yellow hands will hold white hands, and blonde heads will rest on the shoulders of black-haired heads. Sincere breaths come from many small throats.

But people have also seen that when a fourteen- or fifteen-year-old Chinese boy slightly bumped a foreign child while riding a bicycle, more than a dozen foreign children of similar age immediately chased after him, shouting:

"Hit, hit!"

Is it the inspiration of age?

Looking back at those Kuomintang foreign barracks, one feels indignant.

Mr. Juqing (Two) 166

— Ke Ling

Mr. Juqing, over sixty years old, has a wide forehead and a sharp chin, and his facial features resemble a precise triangle: equilateral. A few gray and white whiskers, which don't look very dashing, float on his lips. His eyes are deeply sunken into his cheeks, like two holes. Because he is so small and thin, the gray patriotic cloth sheepskin robe and the black velvet mandarin jacket look particularly bulky. His demeanor and attire clearly tell you that this old man has a history full of vicissitudes.

Yes, everyone in town knows that Mr. Juqing was a successful candidate in the imperial examinations during the Qing Dynasty, had official titles, and was the most knowledgeable tutor in the entire town. Everyone recognized and acknowledged him as such. Moreover, he was surnamed Kong, from a family with a long scholarly tradition, and said to be a direct descendant of Confucius. However, this descendant of the sage is now deeply worried about the reefs ahead of his educational career.

Looking at the few eight or nine students at the Confucius memorial ceremony on the first day of school, he couldn't help but recall the grand occasion of his disciples being like clouds.

Mr. Juqing has been setting up a private school in the town for at least twenty years, sitting on a "cold bench."

Every day teaching "The Master said," "The Book of Songs said," "Zhao, Qian, Sun, Li," accompanied by children often covered in tears and snot, watching bodies swaying like pendulums to the left and right on each desk, ears filled with buzzing sounds of reading, vermilion pens, tracing characters, books, textbooks… These monotonous days are not easy to pass. It can be seen that Mr. Juqing's twenty years have been spent in the midst of this.

Although the life of a teacher is pure and noble, it seems to be a dead end for scholars. In the beginning, how could Mr. Juqing have thought that he would inherit the sacred mission of setting up a school and teaching students?

In his youth, Mr. Juqing, like other scholars buried in their studies at the time, had dreams of wealth and fame swirling in his mind. Because his family was not very well off, he keenly felt the warmth and coldness of human relationships. Thinking of the many impoverished and destitute young masters in unofficial histories and novels, he found that his own situation had many similarities. Therefore, he often expected that his future would be like "a branch of apricot blossoms red for ten miles," bringing glory to his ancestors. Unfortunately, such a beautiful dream was finally shattered along with his withered youth after a dramatic change in the times.

A large number of days passed in an unpleasant state.

Educational News

Guangdong Province Reorganization: Teacher Training and Vocational Education Plans - Intended to Add Three Provincial Normal Schools, Vocational School Departments to be Established Based on Local Needs 180

Recently, the Guangdong Provincial Department of Education has been reorganizing education throughout the province. In addition to changing the names of all provincial secondary schools (as reported previously), it also intends to expand teacher training and vocational education separately. Regarding teacher training, the province will be divided into ten normal school districts: Guangzhou District, Huizhou District, Chaozhou District, Meizhou District, Nan Shao Lian District, Zhao Luo District, Five Counties Two Yang District, Gao Lei District, Qin Lian District, and Qiong Ya District. Each district will establish one normal school for men and one for women. Existing normal schools within the district will have their names corrected, while new schools will be established where none exist. It is noted that the Guangzhou District already has the Provincial First Normal School and the Provincial Women's Normal School. These will continue to operate as before, but the Provincial First Normal School will be renamed the Provincial Jiangcun Normal School, and the Provincial Women's Normal School will become the Guangzhou Women's Normal School. The Huizhou District currently lacks a normal school. It is planned to add a Provincial Lao Long Normal School in Lao Long, Longchuan County. The Chaozhou District has one existing Hanshan Normal School, which will be renamed the Provincial Chaozhou Normal School. The Meizhou District currently lacks a normal school. It is planned to establish a Provincial Xingning Normal School in Xingning County, which belongs to the district. The Nan Shao Lian District has one existing Provincial Third Normal School, which will be renamed the Provincial Zhaoqing Normal School. The Five Counties Two Yang District currently lacks a normal school. It is planned to establish a Provincial Changsha Normal School in Changsha, Kaiping County. The Gao Lei District has one existing Provincial Fifth Normal School, which has already been converted into the Provincial First Agricultural School. The Provincial Tenth Middle School in Leizhou will be converted into the Leizhou Normal School. In the Qin Lian District, the Provincial Twelfth Middle School in Qin County will be converted into the Provincial Qinzhou Normal School. In the Qiong Ya District, the existing Provincial Sixth Normal School will be renamed the Provincial Qiong Ya Normal School. Among the above ten districts, five existing normal schools will be renamed, two middle schools will be converted into normal schools, and three new schools will need to be established.

Regarding vocational education, plans are also being promoted by district. In the Guangzhou District, in addition to correcting the names of the existing Provincial First Vocational School and Provincial Second Agricultural School, it is also planned to establish a Provincial Commercial Vocational School and a Provincial Women's Domestic Vocational School in Guangzhou. In the Huizhou District, it is planned to establish a Provincial Heyuan Agricultural Vocational School in Heyuan, with departments of agronomy and agricultural product manufacturing. In the Chao'an District, it is planned to establish a Provincial Chao'an Industrial Vocational School, with a ceramics department. In the Meizhou District, it is planned to establish a Provincial Xingning Industrial Vocational School in Xingning County. In the Nan Shao Lian District, it is planned to establish a Provincial Shaozhou Agricultural Vocational School in Yingde County, with departments of forestry and horticulture. In the Zhao Luo District, it is planned to establish a Provincial Sihui Agricultural Vocational School in Sihui County, with departments of forestry and agricultural product manufacturing. In the Five Counties Two Yang District, it is planned to establish a Provincial Jiangmen Agricultural Vocational School in Jiangmen, with departments of horticulture and agricultural product manufacturing. In the Gao Lei District, it is planned to establish a Provincial Leizhou Aquatic Products Vocational School in Leizhou. In the Qin Lian District, it is planned to establish a Provincial Qinzhou Industrial Vocational School in Qinzhou, with departments of ceramics and simple chemical industry. In the Qiong Ya District, it is planned to establish a Provincial Nada Agricultural Vocational School in Nada Market, Dan County, with departments of forestry, animal husbandry, horticulture, and agricultural product manufacturing.

Head of Polish School Sailing Ship Pays Respects in Beijing 182

The Polish Minister, Mr. Weidenthal, led the head of the school sailing ship, Mr. Maksymilian Wilkiewicz, and two mates, Mr. Roman Leszczyński, to Beijing on the evening of the 27th to pay respects to the authorities. Four Organizations Jointly Prepare for a Scientific Toy Exhibition - Pan Gongzhan Appointed as Director of Preparations - Exhibition Scheduled to Begin on May 1st 184

The Shanghai Branch of the China Cultural Construction Association, the Shanghai Branch of the Scientific Movement Association, the Children's Welfare Association, and the Citizen Education Center held a preparatory meeting yesterday at the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society to prepare for the Scientific Toy Exhibition in this city. Attendees included Tao Baichuan, Chen Baohua, Zhou Hanmei, and Xu Zhuodai from the Shanghai Branch of the China Cultural Construction Association; Chen Jinmin and Shao Jialin from the Shanghai Branch of the Scientific Movement Association; Qian Fugong from the Children's Welfare Association; and Chen Songchun and Cai Yuanzhan from the Citizen Education Center. Various Circles in This City Prepare to Celebrate Children's Day - Jointly Prepared by the City Party Headquarters and the Welfare Association - Celebration Ceremony Decided to be Held at the Moonlight Theater - All Stores in the City Offer Discounts, All Parks Open to the Public - Hospitals Provide Free Physical Examinations and Smallpox Vaccinations 186

April 4th is the 5th Children's Memorial Day in our country. New Dean of Studies Appointed at Jinan University 190

Dr. Zhai Junqian has been appointed as the Dean of Studies at Jinan University. President Li Ximou resigned from his concurrent position as Dean of Studies because he wanted to concentrate on handling the affairs of the College of Science this semester. President Shen Pengfei repeatedly tried to persuade him to stay but was unsuccessful. He then did his best to find a scholar with rich educational experience to fill the position. Dr. Zhai Junqian has now been appointed. Dr. Zhai is learned and resolute in his work, and has been involved in education for more than ten years. He has served as the Vice President of Jinan University, Director of the Guangzhou Municipal Bureau of Education, and Professor at Peiping University, Zhongshan University in Guangzhou, and various universities in Shanghai. He has long been respected by the scholarly community and has a long history with Jinan University in particular. He successively served as the head professor and vice president of the school for many years. Several years ago, many of the school's expansion and improvement plans came from Dr. Zhai's motion assistance and planning. Now, he has agreed to return to preside over academic affairs, which is truly something to celebrate for the school's future.

Wireless Radio Weekly Supplement of Shen Bao

Testing Low-Frequency Amplification Circuits 203

— Li Yuanqing

When radio repairmen encounter a completely silent radio, the first step is naturally to determine where the problem lies. (Within the rectifier, low-frequency amplifier, intermediate-frequency amplifier, detector, or high-frequency amplifier circuits.) The simplest test method is usually to lightly tap the grid of each vacuum tube (starting from the last tube and moving forward). Listen carefully for popping or buzzing sounds in the speaker. If tapping the grid of a particular vacuum tube produces no sound in the speaker, it indicates that the circuit or vacuum tube is damaged.

While the above testing method is convenient, the confined space and numerous components within a typical radio make it difficult to reach with one's fingers. Even if accessible, it is easy to touch other high-voltage circuits, often resulting in an unexpected shock.

Using a low-frequency oscillator (A.F. Oscillator) to test the low-frequency amplification circuit is, of course, the most thorough method. However, such specialized equipment is expensive and typically reserved for experts. Ordinary amateurs, who prioritize economy, find it difficult to acquire.

Recently, I came across an article in an American radio magazine about a method for testing low-frequency amplification circuits using the alternating current hum from an electric light. It is indeed a novel and practical idea, which I have translated below for fellow enthusiasts.

As shown in the diagram, take a length of floral wire and connect one end to a power outlet. Connect the other end in series with a 0.0005 MFD fixed capacitor capable of withstanding high voltage, and then connect it to a test prod. (The test prod resembles a regular mechanical pencil, with the upper part made of insulating material and the lower tip a conductor, as shown in the dotted box in the upper left corner of the attached diagram.) During use, first plug the wire into the electric light outlet and turn on the radio. Then, touch the test prod to the plate and grid of the power amplification tube (as shown by dotted lines 1 and 2 in the diagram). If a humming AC sound is heard in the speaker, it indicates that the final-stage low-frequency amplification circuit is intact. Repeat this process, touching the plate and grid of each vacuum tube in sequence until no AC sound is produced in the speaker. This will identify the location of the damaged low-frequency amplification stage.

Knowledge for Beginners 204

— Yang Xuelun

Instructions for beginners on assembling radios have already appeared in various issues of this publication, so there seems to be no need to repeat them. However, a close reading of previous articles reveals that most focus on the assembly of single-tube radios. Given the current variety of vacuum tube types and numbers, there are also many circuit diagrams. Even when there is a description of vacuum tube selection, it is often vague, leaving beginners confused and uncertain. Therefore, I am using this space to share some advice for fellow beginners in radio.

Those who study radio typically start with crystal radios and, after some time, find their efficiency too low. They then upgrade to single-tube, then two-tube radios, and so on. However, due to a lack of sufficient knowledge, purchased vacuum tubes and components are discarded, and circuits are repeatedly modified, wasting beginners' money and time. I have organized my findings into a systematic account so that beginners can avoid groping in the dark and feeling lost.

(1) Power Supply: The most important and first issue to resolve when assembling a radio is the power supply. In prosperous cities, most power plants supply AC electricity, so it is best to use an AC power supply. Although the initial investment is slightly higher, the ongoing expense of DC batteries far exceeds the electricity bill for an AC unit. However, AC power is drawn from high-voltage currents, so caution is advised for those without significant knowledge of electricity. I suggest that beginners start by assembling a semi-AC radio, paying close attention to the primary two-wire terminals and avoiding touching them. Once sufficient experience is gained, then try assembling a full AC radio. In remote towns and cities, or places where power plants do not supply daytime electricity, a DC power supply is preferable.

(2) Vacuum Tubes: Vacuum tubes hold a primary position in radio, so after deciding on the power supply, the next step is to select the type and number of vacuum tubes to match the power supply and other components to their characteristics. Although vacuum tube manufacturing in Europe and America is constantly innovating, with more and more tubes being produced, each has its specific function and cannot be interchanged. Therefore, expansion should be considered from the beginning of assembly to avoid discarding initially purchased tubes. After research by myself and other amateurs, the most economical and durable vacuum tubes for DC are 30, 32, 33, 34, and for AC are 36, 38, 39, 77, 78, etc. (To be continued)

Improved Earphone Magnetization 205

— Chen Binhui

A demagnetized earphone loses its effectiveness. Various radio publications often describe methods for magnetization, typically involving briefly touching the two terminals of the earphone to the positive and negative poles of a high-voltage source to restore its magnetism. However, my experiments have revealed areas for improvement, which I will describe below.

My Erpees earphone (made in Germany) has been used for over two years, and its magnetism has gradually diminished. Following the aforementioned method, I briefly touched the two terminals of the earphone to the positive and negative poles of a B battery. With a click, the magnetism of one side of the earphone was very strong, but the other side completely lost its magnetism (both sides were originally balanced). I then reversed the terminals and touched them again, with the opposite result. In short, I could only fully magnetize one side at a time. I then unscrewed the Bakelite cover of the earphone, removed the steel diaphragm, and unsoldered the terminals of the A and B wires, connecting them to longer wires (as shown in Figure 1) to magnetize them separately (if ineffective, reverse the two ends of the wire). This allows both sides of the earphone to restore their original magnetism, avoiding the aforementioned problem.

Diode Triode Vacuum Tube Voltmeter 206

— Chongling

(Continued from issue 106)

If we want to measure the maximum value of the input AC voltage, we can insert a variable battery E in addition to the fixed C battery in the grid circuit of Figure 1, and connect a DC voltmeter V to it to measure the negative voltage of E, as shown in Figure 3. When there is no voltage input, the value of E should be zero (that is, the voltage indicated by the V voltmeter is zero). At this time, there is only a negative voltage C in the grid circuit, and the MA ammeter only shows a small amount of current. If there is a voltage input, the plate current will inevitably increase. Therefore, the grid negative voltage E can be increased until the plate current returns to its original value (that is, the plate current when there is no voltage input). At this time, the voltage indicated by the V voltmeter is the increased negative voltage in the grid circuit: the value of this negative voltage is equal to the maximum value of the input voltage. Therefore, the voltage measured by V is the maximum value of the input voltage.

(2) The grid-detector vacuum tube voltmeter uses a grid-detector circuit, as shown in Figure 4. Cg is the grid capacitor, Rg is the grid leak, C is the bypass capacitor, and E is the balancing battery. Since this circuit does not have a C battery in the grid circuit, when there is no voltage input in the grid circuit, the plate still has a considerable DC current. The voltage of E can be increased to reduce the current of the MA ammeter until the DC current shown by MA is exactly zero. If an external voltage is input to the grid circuit, the plate current will inevitably change, and the voltage of E will lose its balancing effect. Then the changed plate current flows through MA, and the pointer of MA will turn to a corresponding position. The current shown by MA can measure the value of the input voltage.

The grid-detector vacuum tube voltmeter is more sensitive than the plate-detector type for measuring low AC voltages, but it consumes more power, and the plate current is quite large when there is no voltage input. Therefore, the grid-detector type is not as good as the plate-detector type unless extremely high sensitivity is required.

In general, the vacuum tube voltmeter is superior to the ordinary voltmeter in the following two aspects:

(1) Its own power consumption is extremely low, so measuring the voltage of a certain circuit with it will not disturb the current of this circuit.

(2) If the bypass capacitor of its plate circuit is configured properly, it will be independent of the frequency of the measured voltage. Therefore, a vacuum tube voltmeter calibrated with low frequency can also be used to measure high frequency voltage.

Five years ago, a certain university professor said, "Once the examination system is implemented, qualified people will have food to eat." But today, that statement is not necessarily true. A certain important person put it more bluntly, saying, "What qualifications? One word from me is the qualification."

Liberation means breaking free from the constraints of the old morality, and absolute freedom in all actions.
