Sketching from Life 208

— Yanqiao

In ancient China, painting and writing were one and the same. A character was a painting, and a painting was a character. Later, painting progressed and progressed from realism to symbolism. The Song Dynasty painting academy used poetry as themes, leading painters towards artistry, and sketching from life was no longer valued by painters. By the Qing Dynasty, the Four Wangs focused on landscape paintings. Fortunately, there was Yun Nantian, who created a new path and showed his genius in realism, competing with the Four Wangs and reviving sketching from life in China.

Unfortunately, sketching from life did not receive the promotion of connoisseurs, and successors were few, and therefore still regarded as a minor art. In modern times, the world trend tends towards realism, and sketching from life has risen again. We have several painters in Suzhou who can express their artistic essence, such as Cheng Yaosheng, who has left Suzhou for Shanghai, is a representative. Chen Jia, who is still in Suzhou, and his disciple Liu Junran, can carry on his legacy. Jia's sketches are not only lifelike, but also his compositions are lively and innovative. Recently, he finished a painting "Chicks under Flowers." Half of the painting is a rose, full of vitality, and the other half depicts seven chicks, downy, lively, symbolizing a kindergarten. This painting was exhibited in the Zheng She Capital Painting Exhibition and received much praise. Later, Mrs. Chen Bijun bought it for sixty yuan. Now Jia has repainted it, even more charming. He also painted "Purple Wisteria and Ducklings," depicting the poetic warmth of the spring river, and having the same mystery as Weng Xiaohai of Wujiang a hundred years ago. (Weng was best at sketching from life and was known as Weng Turtle.) Junran's paintings of flowers, fruits, and vegetables are also unique. It is said that the teacher and student are going to exhibit at the Literary Society in Shanghai and Hankou. Such sketches with scientific mind and literary skill will surely return with glory.

Finally, I would also like to report a news: Cheng Xiaoqing, famous for the Hawthorne detective cases, is also Jia's star pupil, and will have "Fish Pleasure" and plum blossom feathers, etc., as embellishments for novelists' paintings, or will be especially appreciated by people.

Liu'an Tea 209

— Teabowl

It is said that tea is extremely addictive, and those who like to drink tea will become addicted. I am one of those who are addicted. I did not drink much tea before, but now I am madly in love with it, and I can't do without it every day!

But my love is exclusive: I only drink Liu'an tea, not other teas: Wuyi, Qimen, Longjing, Dongting... Although I have had love affairs with them, the result is that the whole of me is occupied by Liu'an tea. No matter what tea it is, I don't think it has the taste of Liu'an tea, nor is it as gentle, handsome, soft, spicy, and coquettish!

I often compare ancient beauties to tea. Liu'an tea is as beautiful and as unfortunate as Wang Zhaojun. Liu'an tea, except for a very small amount sold in northern Anhui, is almost entirely sold by the Shandong gang to the northern provinces. After they transport it there, they use jasmine to make scented tea, completely covering up its original appearance. The way northerners drink tea is even crueler. Large teapots are famous. They stuff handfuls of leaves into the pot, pour them into large bowls, and drink them. It's like Wang Zhaojun talking about the love of cohabitation with a foreign king with a beard like a halberd, which is the same thing as burning a zither and boiling a crane!

Occasionally, Liu'an tea also comes to the South, but the southerners are used to being fascinated by Longjing tea, which is like Xi Shi. Who cares about Wang Zhaojun! Probably the Liu'an tea that comes to the South, although not fake, is all inferior. I can't buy really good Liu'an tea in Shanghai.

Really good Liu'an tea, one flag and one gun, color, aroma, and taste, are all above Longjing. Especially "Ban Zhen," after being slightly boiled, the fragrance is sweet and fragrant, how can it not make people drunk for three days? Back to the topic, tea is like a woman, Longjing is a yarn-washing girl; Biluochun is a miss; Ban Zhen is a dignified, mature young mistress; if you are a sick Sima Xiangru, and really want to relieve your thirst, you must pursue the young mistress, right?

Work hard! To level the bumpy road of this world.

Little Western Paradise 210

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 11: A Sad Nighttime Conversation About Life Being a Dream; Footprints Scattered, The Wind and Rain Too Deceiving

But finding that position as a concubine isn't something you can jump into. You still have to run to Little Western Paradise for a few months first. This young lady from my hometown, she saw her sisters all doing it this way. What was there that she couldn't do? Suddenly, she also caught the disease of going to Little Western Paradise. You have to give her credit, though. In less than half a month, she had new clothes, leather shoes, and a watch. Someone took her to see Shaanxi opera. She was almost to the point of riding in a private mule cart. It was then that she met a male compatriot who took her to Kaifeng for half a year. It seems that male compatriot didn't want her anymore, so she had to return to Shaanxi. But having been to the East, she was even more modern. She needed money for herself, and her family needed money, so she had to run to Little Western Paradise again, using her body to exchange for money. But her husband's family was a conservative family. How could they tolerate this? So they broke off the engagement. Although she hadn't returned to her old home in Jiangnan, she had been to Kaifeng, which was several times more prosperous than Xi'an. She knew how comfortable it was to be a concubine in the East. She used to think that riding in a private mule cart with a uniformed servant was a big deal, but now she knew that it was nothing to boast about. But even though she looked down on people in her heart, she still had to humor those who looked down on her in order to have food to eat, clothes to wear, and an opium habit to satisfy. That's how I am. But I thought about it, and I absolutely couldn't continue doing things without shame. To be honest, selling your body is selling a little bit of beauty, selling a little bit of youth. I'm getting older every day. It's getting harder and harder for me. If I keep humoring them, I'll definitely starve to death in Xi'an and won't be able to return to my hometown. Speaking of this, her voice choked again, as if she couldn't go on. But she immediately thought that it was meaningless to cry to people all the time. So she stood up to pour tea, offered the guest a cup, and drank a cup herself, changing the subject and moving on. (170)

The Fragrant Record of the Imperial Incense 211

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

The residence occupied by these silk-making artisans is not small. Generally, it consists of a central main hall with two rows of side halls on both sides. As for the carved beams, painted pillars, and flying pavilions, they are exactly the same as the rest of the place. Such a spacious and magnificent workshop can be said to be rare in the world, no wonder the girls are so happy that they forget their homes! They work in the central main halls during the day and return to the side halls of the two emperors to rest at night. Their lives are extremely orderly.

Now let me briefly talk about some of the official silk-making procedures. The reeled raw silk is sorted into skeins, then washed and dried in the sun, and then dyed in various colors. Dyeing is certainly not done once; it must be dyed two or three times before finally being taken out to dry in the sun. Near the side halls where they live, there is a stone flat, which is where the silk is dried. When drying the silk, many bamboo tripods must also be used; their height is not very high, because if they are too high, the girls will not be able to reach them. In the middle of every two tripods, there is a very smooth bamboo pole; the dyed silk is hung on it in skeins to dry, but things are not that simple! At the beginning of drying, the direction of sunlight must first be observed. The silk cannot be half exposed to sunlight and half not exposed to sunlight. After a considerable period of time, they must be turned over or moved to ensure that the time they are exposed to light is very uniform, so that the color of the silk will not be dark in one part and light in another. (281)

Old Tales of Fengyang 212

— Yin Er

Since the premiere of the New Women's Film, the Fengyang songbook has been almost universally sung, depicting rural bankruptcy, chaos, famine, making people unwilling to sing, and whether Fengyang is originally a good place is also worth studying. According to Fengyang, formerly known as Haozhou, the Fengyang government was established at the beginning of the Ming Dynasty. The Qing Dynasty followed it and belonged to Anhui Province. The Republic of China abolished the government and kept the county, and it was governed by the Huaisi Road of Anhui. Recently, I read Gu Danhu's (Danwu) Xiaoxia Xianji excerpts, about the situation in Fengyang in the early Ming Dynasty, knowing that the Ming Taizu wanted to prosper Fengyang but could not get it. Taizu originally rose in Fengyang, because he thought it was an auspicious place, so he worked hard to govern it, but after the chaos, there were few people and the land was barren, so he moved 140,000 wealthy households from Jiangnan to fill it. Those who returned privately were punished. He also set up egg households, fishing households, and teaching workshops, etc., and imprisoned the sons, grandsons, wives, and daughters of ministers of enemy countries and sent them all to the teaching workshops, entering the Pingkang Courtyard as prostitutes. These are not the ways to cultivate the original intention. According to legend, wealthy people who wanted to return to their hometown to visit their tombs would often disguise themselves as beggars, men and women, and secretly return to worship. They would go in winter and return in spring, which became a custom, and they had to go when the time came, which was far from the original intention of visiting the tomb.

Lament for Ruan Lingyu 213

— (Xuan)

The moth-brow weeps, composing a song of a toothless rat, shaming the spring heart falling between two homes. Knowing that she died because of love, her grave will not grow a mimosa flower.

Grief and fear, like a drama, vex the beauty. It is said that she was smart but stubborn. She has taken away all the romance, but still leaves the tears and smiles in the world.

A Call to Laughter

— (Qingyun)

Because laughter is, after all, an expression of joy. Even in tragic circumstances, perhaps because of the mixture of knowledge, the power of sorrow becomes even more deeply ingrained in people's hearts. Like Charlie Chaplin's comedies on the screen, the endless laughter contains profound sorrow, much like drinking a strong cup of coffee, the bitter taste felt at the end. However, precisely because of this bitter taste, people can feel excited and feel that this laughter has a deep and long taste that can be chewed on! The following are a few examples of jokes.

Expensive Brush and Ink: A scholar in the past wrote characters that were like earthworms crawling and meaningless, but he thought they were like dragons and snakes dancing, with a unique charm, and he actually shamelessly started a career as a calligrapher selling characters for a living. He knew that his own characters could scare the vulgar but could not deceive the knowledgeable, so he had a brilliant idea. His fees specifically promoted the brush and ink he used, such as Song Dynasty wolf hair, Ming Dynasty goose pen, and so on, with many names. As for ancient ink, there were even more names and expensive prices. One day, this great calligrapher, in order to promote himself, specially wrote a pair of couplets and asked a famous contemporary person to comment on them. That famous person looked at his handwriting and then looked at his fees, and unhesitatingly inscribed five large characters: "Expensive Brush and Ink."

Awarded to Me: When Emperor Qianlong visited the Lion Grove Garden, he was overjoyed and wrote the three characters "Really Interesting" in imperial calligraphy. Fortunately, his minister Gao Shiqi was tactful and asked for the word "Interesting." This ungrammatical inscription did not taint the scenic spot. In the midst of organizing scenic spots and promoting scenery, a group of gentlemen who were fond of elegance would also occasionally make the "Really Interesting" joke with their enthusiastic inscriptions. In the midst of organizing Tiger Hill, a famous person proposed the four characters "Ancient Wu Overlooking the Scenery" for the front gate. An editor of a certain newspaper felt that the word "Overlooking" was "awarded to me" and wrote two other words "Scenery" and "Traces" for exchange, asking him to change it to "Ancient Wu Beautiful Scenery" or "Ancient Wu Historical Traces."

Progress of Learning: There was a scholar in the past who took a fancy to a wine-selling daughter. He wrote many rhyming love letters and sent them one after another, but it seemed like a stone sinking into the sea, with no reply at all. It was not until the scholar became lovesick and was dying that his servant wrote a letter full of typos and sent it. Only then did the daughter rush over that night. The scholar received it and, in joy, asked her why she had not come the previous times. The daughter smiled and said, "The previous letters you sent were unreadable, and I knew your learning was still not good! Today's letter is completely clear at a glance, how can it not make people feel pity and love, so I hurried to see you." The scholar listened and was so angry that his eyes straightened and his feet stiffened, and he died.

I Am the Only One: When a certain literary figure was lecturing on the stage, he criticized the famous writers of ancient and modern times one by one, saying that they were all worthless. At this time, a student listening to the lecture became angry and stood up and asked: You said that ancient and modern writers are not good, so the best writer is naturally only you, sir? The literary figure listened and nodded frequently and said, "Indeed! Indeed!" At this time, there was a burst of enthusiastic laughter from the audience.

Shanghai Local Supplement of Shen Bao

Talk

A Gentleman Keeps Away from the Kitchen 214

— Chen Liang

When I was a child, I was confined in the "Old French School" to study ancient books, reciting without explanation. Therefore, I failed to grasp the meaning of various "aphorisms" and "quatrains," passing over them vaguely. Later, I regretted it deeply, but I still thought of catching up quickly. I often flipped through the large-character woodblock books and was willing to study the sayings of the ancients. Over time, I inevitably gained some understanding, but what followed closely behind the understanding was still confusion and wonder, which was extremely frustrating.

For example, I recently came across the saying "A gentleman keeps away from the kitchen," which made me ponder it quite a bit. According to the meaning in the books, it says that a gentleman has a sense of compassion. He cannot bear to hear the cooks and stewards slaughtering and killing in the kitchen, and the miserable cries of those chickens, sheep, and livestock when their necks are spurting blood. Therefore, he sits a little further away to avoid feeling depressed and losing his joy. The problem is originally very simple. However, precisely because it is too simple, it easily stimulates my brain.

It's not that I have any aversion to the humanitarianism of the "gentleman keeps away from the kitchen" faction. What I want to ask now is, who makes the killing and harming actions in the gentleman's kitchen happen, who causes them? I think a cook or steward would never slaughter a pig for no reason if the master didn't eat meat. Moreover, according to research, it was rare for ancient gentlemen not to eat meat. So, if they ate the meat, why couldn't they bear to hear the sound? You are determined to shoot your enemy to death, but you still proclaim that you cannot bear to see your enemy bleed. What kind of talk is that! Thinking like this, ancient gentlemen were good at pretending everywhere, good at wearing masks. The so-called humanity is just a layer of sugar coating on a poisonous pill.

However, is it only ancient gentlemen who are like this? Aren't today's gentlemen the same? Their faces are hypocritical, their methods are clever, and they often shout at the top of their lungs: "I universally care for all beings, I passionately love peace, I will always be a good person..." But in their two hands, one is a mixture of sugar and anesthetics, and the other holds the sharpest butcher knife. Or, they themselves are engrossed in the work of a cook. When you become the meat on their chopping board, they open their bloody mouths wide: "Haha, you just didn't make enough effort." After swallowing you in one gulp, they are still gentlemen, and they will still say: "I cannot bear to kill and harm." In fact, they are still standing at the door of the kitchen.

Perhaps humans are born with a talent for deceiving, and at the same time, humans willingly accept deception, dying without complaint. Otherwise, why has this kind of deceptive trick like "A gentleman keeps away from the kitchen" become even more intensified today?

Passing Through the Xiamen Strait by Boat 215

— Kong Ming

As the ship was about to enter the Xiamen Strait, it was restrained from afar by the continuous mountain range. The ship slowly crawled forward, and on the waves reflecting the sky, fishing boats hoisted their giant sails in groups, fluttering on the sea. When they got close to the ship, the fishermen's dark faces and strong arms could be clearly seen. In the distance, the ridges of the mountains were illuminated by the sun, fully revealing their blue and bright faces. In some mountain recesses, the villages formed by the fishermen were hidden by deep green trees, forming small piles of shadows.

Seabirds followed the stern of the ship from the distant sea. Once it entered the strait, the flock of birds gathered more and more. The stern of the ship stirred up a long strip of white waves on the sea, and the light blue surface was full of white foam. The flocks of birds forever stared at these white foams with hatred in their eyes. Then, they suddenly plunged into the sea with their sharp beaks, and immediately lifted up a fish, slowly swallowing it into their mouths. After that, they continued to soar behind the ship, constantly spinning around, without feeling tired at all, until the sound of the ship's engine stopped.

From the first time I saw the mountains of Xiamen, the water journey to Xiamen and Gulangyu was not very short. I kept seeing mountains and the sea, which was restrained like a river. It took two hours to reach Xiamen. The ship initially went around the back of Gulangyu. As soon as I saw the white lighthouse building in the daylight, the dense Western-style houses of Gulangyu appeared. The colors were exceptionally bright and neat, and when they were set off by the green trees and reflected in the sunlight, the beautiful island floated up from the sea. The scenery felt very beautiful, and the passengers all leaned out to stare at the beautiful island.

The ship turned around from the back of Gulangyu, and the front view was presented with an even more majestic and beautiful face. The houses were even more densely packed and stood even taller? Many red brick walls, matched with dense windows, directly confronted Xiamen. Looking at the situation, it really seemed like imperialism was constantly provoking China's gateway - Xiamen?

Then the city of Xiamen showed itself in a new posture. On the coast, a long row of tall Western houses stood completely with white walls. As the ship approached, the signs of ×× Foreign Company or ×× Hotel waved at the travelers with large letters. In the gaps between the large houses, the streets spewed out their big mouths. The rumbling of cars and the ringing of rickshaws were all transmitted from the air. And the noise of the city was刺着travelers' nerves again.

When the night boat docked in Xiamen, the lights of Gulangyu twinkled from the mountainside, as dense as the stars in the sky. The sounds of Xiamen were exceptionally noisy. Compared with the tranquility of the opposite shore, it was like dividing into two worlds. In the evening, the sound of small boats rowing could be heard everywhere, occasionally mixed with one or two whistles, brushing through the water space, which really made people feel as if they were in the water village of Venice!

The moonlight was reflected on the water, and the sea was filled with a white light. The lights of the small boats were as lonely as fireflies, and compared with the electric lights on both sides, they were like fireflies compared to kerosene lamps.

The next morning, the ship departed from the Xiamen Strait again. Slowly peeling away from the shore, the small burdens of the vendors all slipped off the ship, and the shouts of hawking disappeared. The beautiful scenery of Gulangyu gradually faded from sight, the ship stirred up a long strip of white foam on the sea again, and the seabirds flew in groups again, forever circling behind the ship.

After bypassing Gulangyu again, it was restrained between the two rows of mountains. I didn't know how much time had passed until I slipped out of the sea off Dingguang, and the seabirds had disappeared unnoticed.

Return 216

— Ming

The night after receiving a letter from a friend saying he was returning to Shanghai, my old classmate of seven years unexpectedly and quickly visited me. In joy and surprise, we shook hands tightly, speechless for a long time, as if we were mutually understanding the comfort of loneliness: just like when we lived together before.

After we graduated, I quickly found a position in an office, but he, on the contrary, ran into walls everywhere. Like a pure young man who had just stepped out of the school gate, he deeply felt disappointment. He almost lost his ambition to progress. At this time, I set up a berth for him in my cramped upstairs room, and he slept on the bed all day, without thinking, as if this was the meaning of his existence. When I returned home after work, I saw his blank face – and also felt that my own profession was precarious, so I couldn't think of a word of comfort or encouragement. This lonely life extended until he entered his uncle's compradore firm.

Originally, this was a very good path, but perhaps because he was a university student, he didn't think that eating required shortcuts other than his knowledge. I remember after finishing his first day of work, he told me that if it weren't for his uncle's sincerity, he would never want to do this kind of mechanical thing. He felt that society was not at all what he had imagined in school. It was opening its poisonous mouth to devour every young and pure heart! But his experienced uncle, after seeing through his disappointment, used the entire commercial textbook to teach him, so that he could understand the art of eating.

Under the influence of this kind of learning, valuable new phenomena also unfolded in our cramped room. If life can be divided into two segments, we had stepped into another class to experience life.

A year later, his uncle bought a branch factory in Huaibei, and he took on the important responsibility of monitoring the actions of the factory manager and separated from me. This was in the winter of the year before last.

At first, I often read his letters. He told me many of the folk customs and living conditions in the north. He said that there was the society of his dreams. He wanted to work hard and repay his uncle for giving him the opportunity to be a person again. I rejoiced that my old friend had a good opportunity, and all the words I hadn't thought of before were conveyed to him in the letters.

After last summer, his letters became sparse, or were just short greetings. He wanted me to send more Shanghai publications and a newspaper – there was no second newspaper in the entire county besides the police station – to relieve his loneliness. So I ran to Sima Road for two days and ordered three publications for him, and selected a dozen books that could be read – the ones I thought were a little better on my bookshelf – and sent them to him one after another.

At the end of the year, he returned to Shanghai. I received the date of his arrival in Shanghai and went to the station to meet him, but a young man who had gone to the ideal society to work hard had completely changed, he had become an insensible shell. He cried, his efforts had been wasted in the techniques of petty merchants, and he had spent the last few months living a life of prostitution and heavy drinking, so that he would not commit suicide. But he didn't want his uncle to know, so he returned to Huaibei in tears this spring. For three months, I haven't received a second letter from him besides one saying he arrived safely on the road.

This time, after our unexpected return and meeting, the first sentence he said to me was: "I'm unemployed!"

Naturally, this fruit had matured before it bloomed. It was the ending that a university student who wanted to adapt to the environment with the textbooks from school deserved. This society is exactly the opposite of what we imagined! If you don't want to dye yourself into a multicolored cloth, unemployment will forever follow you like a shadow!

I looked at his insensible face and swallowed the words that were surging in my throat.

The Drunkard Ma Sanzi 217

— Chunyun

The fire pot-like sun quietly sank behind the rubber plantation in the west. The wind swept in gusts from the rubber plantation, mixed with a bit of the rubber's fragrance, stinging people's nostrils.

At this time, the workers in the rubber plantation, laughing and joking, received the reward for their day's labor from the accounting office. They seemed to have forgotten the fatigue of the day's work, forgotten the dirt beads oozing from their black charcoal-like faces, and forgotten the upper half of their clothes that had been soaked through with sweat, as if they had been lifted out of the water, dripping with water. They walked in groups into the Yongxing "local boss"'s tavern, forgetting everything, and happily drinking three or five cups.

The Yongxing "local boss"'s tavern was opened on the right side of the rubber plantation. The customers in the tavern were naturally the workers in the rubber plantation. The tavern was about two zhang wide, and so low that you could touch the roof with a hand. The roof was made of "attap" leaves. When the wind swept over, it made a rustling sound. There were also two tall palm trees outside the tavern, like two flagpoles standing tall, but they lacked the two wine flags fluttering above.

Every day, when the sun sank behind the rubber country in the west, the Yongxing "local boss"'s tavern's business became prosperous. Yongxing "local boss" stood in front of the counter, waving a fan in his hand, sticking out his bulging belly, and greeting customers with a smiling face. The tables inside the tavern were occupied by many workers who were as black as ghosts, drinking wine and talking loudly about the novel news that had happened in the rubber plantation.

Ma Sanzi, with a face full of honeycomb-like spots, staggered out of the rubber plantation. From a distance, Yongxing "local boss" greeted him. He was also one of the tavern's main customers, and he had to come to the tavern every day to drink three or five cups.

When Ma Sanzi's shadow flashed in, many workers inside, as soon as they saw him, grinned and made faces at him, saying in a mocking tone:

"Ma Sanzi, did the foreman give you more wages today?"

"Of course! Letting your wife sleep with the foreman, how could you not get benefits?" another person chimed in.

"Ma Sanzi, ask her to sleep with us once, will that work?" Then, everyone in the tavern laughed.

In this kind of situation, Ma Sanzi really didn't know whether to laugh or cry. He wanted to make trouble with them, but it didn't seem to make any sense, and if things got out of hand, it would be like opening a toilet lid in the wind, the stench would spread even further, which wouldn't be worth it; but silence was close to showing weakness! In the end, he also answered with a semi-humorous tone.

"I have never put women in my eyes... you fuck your mother, what's the problem with sleeping with you once!" Then he raised his hand and heavily knocked his fist on the table. "'Local boss'! Come on, a plate of dried fish and two catties of white wine." It seemed that in this way, the pent-up anger in his stomach would be completely vented.

While Ma Sanzi drank the wine, he was very unhappy in his heart. Although his mouth kept saying "I don't put women in my eyes," it was a kind of shame for him no matter what if a woman slept with someone else! He poured the wine cup after cup into his stomach, two catties passed and then two more catties were added, until the "attap" roof was spinning, and his eyes were full of red threads, like two red balls, and the wine glass was too heavy to lift, before he staggered out of the tavern door.

When Ma Sanzi staggered to the door of his home, his woman ran out from inside, supporting his rough arms and saying:

"Oh dear! You went to drink again, and you're so drunk!"...

"Bitch! You did a good deed, I won't let you off today!..." His anger, which had been闷in his stomach, swelled up again when he saw his woman. He grabbed her short hair and delivered many heavy slaps like raindrops.

Then, his woman cried哇啦哇啦. But he fell to the floor and slept soundly, like a pile of mud.

Classical Prose 220

Wang Bingmei, Donglai's Broad Deliberations

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM

"Willing to Kao Shu Fight for the Chariot" (Continued)

Xun Kao Shu pushed the respect for his parents as the respect for the ancestral temple. He certainly would not dare to fight for the chariot in the Grand Palace. 推事親之肅. 为军旅之肃.必不敢挟赖于大逵矣. Only because he cannot promote it, he initially obtained the name of pure filial piety, but in the end, he could not avoid the warning of urging his parents to be in danger. Or said, Kao Shu's attack on Xu, took the lead with lightness, could it also not promote his filial piety? Said, fighting for the chariot is private. Not filial. Taking the lead is public. Filial. Loving his body is filial piety to his parents. Forgetting his body is loyalty to his monarch. How can loyalty and filial piety have two first principles? Zeng Zi considered war without courage to be unfilial, then Kao Shu's courage is exactly what Zeng Zi called filial piety. However, he did not die from the injury of taking the lead, but died from Zidu's shot. Dying in private and not dying in public. This is why I deeply regret his inability to promote it. Broadcasting News 221

The Shanghai Zacao Society is an organization formed by young art enthusiasts in Shanghai after their studies. Led by Mr. Wu Xiongjian, with the cooperation of Chen Liang, Wang Dasu, Zhu Tingyun, Xia Zhonghan, Liu Tongkang, Li Tianfeng, and others, it is now scheduled to broadcast a special drama program every Sunday afternoon from 6:00 to 7:00 p.m. on the New Sound Radio Station (frequency 1380), starting from the 31st of this month. It is said that most of the scripts are self-written and directed by the society, focusing on promoting the national spirit and advocating the New Life Movement. It is expected to be a feast for the ears of the audience at that time.

Shen Bao Shanghai Local Supplement Film Special

Recollections of a Famous Soviet Film Seen Six or Seven Years Ago 222

— Ang Ge

The Soviet Union's International Film Festival has opened. China has also selected seven famous films to participate, and Ms. Hu Die, along with Ambassador Yan and Mei Lanfang, have traveled to Russia. Therefore, people's attention has turned to the Soviet Union, especially its films.

This reminds me of several Soviet films I saw six or seven years ago. At that time, I followed my father and lived in a small town in Latvia near the Soviet border. We often saw Soviet films.

The first film I saw, and the one that still leaves an indelible impression, is a tragic film called "A Country Girl from Liangshang Province."

The protagonist of the film, the country girl, was played by the Soviet actress Trecha Ersajia. The background is a typical Russian farm.

The plot is as follows: A peasant family in Liangshang Province, a father and son, live a very happy life. There is a young girl in the village, and both father and son like her very much. Eventually, the son and she fall in love and get married.

But not long after the wedding, the son is drafted by the revolutionary government to participate in the domestic war. He is gone for three or four years, and there is no news from him during this time. The father at this time rapes his daughter-in-law, and coincidentally, the daughter-in-law becomes pregnant.

The relationship between father-in-law and daughter-in-law is forced. She still expects her husband to return. However, her belly grows larger, and a son is born. What can she do? She feels mental pain and cries day and night. Fortunately, her sister-in-law treats her well and comforts her.

Finally, the war stops, but the son did not die on the battlefield. He happily returns home. He imagines all the way: his father will shed tears of joy when he sees him; his beloved wife will certainly kiss him, maybe scream hysterically, and tell him the story of the past few years with mixed feelings of sadness and joy, which will naturally be the happiest.

When he gets home, ah! The situation is not as he imagined. The family is silent when they see him return! The father, with a guilty conscience, coldly runs away. The wife is holding a child in her arms. When she sees him, she only looks at the ground, silently shedding tears.

He understands, is disappointed, and is resentful. Without saying a word, he beats his wife. What can the wife say in this situation? Bearing the pain of body and mind, she runs out of the house. It is very lively outside, and the villagers are having a festival to enjoy themselves, but this only highlights her loneliness. She sits alone on a rock by the stream, blankly, her eyes full of tears, and the wind blows, raising her soft black hair; she also sprinkles drops of tears into the flowing water at her feet. When the tears are gone, she jumps into the deep stream.

People clamor: the son is also awakened from his pain by this sound and runs out of the house. Neighbors have already placed the dead woman by the stream. Her black hair is scattered, and her beautiful face is as pale as wax; but it is also shining brightly. The son cannot help but kneel down, holding the corpse and crying bitterly.

The onlookers are all around, and the old women are busy making the sign of the cross and praying to God. The honest farmers are all shedding tears of sympathy for this bizarre tragedy. After a while, the son raises his head and sees his father standing in the crowd with tears in his eyes, his face full of regret and shame. At this time, the son's face shows an unspeakable hatred!

The plot is so gentle and profound that it has won the tears of countless infatuated men and women. I have seen it for six or seven years, but as long as I think of it, I always feel a slight sourness in my heart! No wonder this film has been playing for many years and still has the ability to draw crowds.

Film Review

Review of "Murder in the Clouds" 223

— Chan Fei

Murder in the Clouds

— Grand Theater

Generally, detective films cannot be separated from thieves and police. The thieves are vicious and also clever and cunning, but in the end, they cannot escape the hands of the police. When they fall into the net of the law, the wicked will naturally be punished. As mentioned above, this is almost the formula for general detective films, and "Murder in the Clouds" is no exception. As for the male protagonist succeeding and love being fulfilled, it is also a necessary insertion in general mediocre detective films.

For such a vulgar film, we have almost nothing to say. Such a formulaic plot structure is probably familiar to those who often watch films.

The positive side here is naturally to advise people not to be robbers, but the opposite effect is that the large-scale organization and equipment of the robbers are a terrible temptation for those who take risks. Of course, we are not saying that there would be no robbers without films that teach robbery. The scientification of robber activity is a characteristic of modern society. But in the end, there is inevitably something close to piracy, although the screenwriter's original intention is to vigorously promote the strictness of the national police organization and imply the security of American society.

Because of the strong stimulation, filmmakers regard it as a way to make money. Under this intention, "Murder in the Clouds" uses the transportation of military supplies by plane as the main scene. The sound of planes and the sound of bullets are dangerous and terrifying. However, because the director and performers are mediocre and incompetent, they did not achieve as good results as they expected. As for pointing out which scenes are better and which places are bad, it seems redundant. Frankly speaking, this film cannot make people feel much interest, it is just a mediocre work.

Review of "Pirate Treasure" 224

— Hua Lun

"Pirate Treasure"

—— Carlton Theater

This is a film with an extremely long story, and other than the thrilling performances of fighting, fleeing and chasing, falling and jumping, there doesn't seem to be anything else to it, a martial arts film.

The aviator Dick announced that he would go to a certain island to excavate the pearls buried by his ancestors. A lawyer, Black, heard about it and sent a group of capable subordinates to steal Dick's treasure island map. Then, following the stealing and grabbing of this map, the protagonist Dick fought back and forth with this group of people, fighting a big battle.

The whole film has seven or eight long scenes of fighting, mostly Dick fighting with his bare hands and single-handedly against a large group of people. He is free to come and go in the air and in the water, and his skills are so high that people can't help but exclaim "amazing!" and have the feeling of ancient Chinese swordsmen. But what is unbelievable is that Dick, as a nationally admired aviator, aviation, often accompanied by famous ladies like Miss Dorothy, and also consulted with Captain Carson on important matters, is a famous figure, how can he always be entangled by the people sent by the bad lawyer and engage in the business of seeking wealth and killing lives? How can he not alarm the government? In broad daylight, Dick was knocked down from the fifth floor, and the police maintaining order only lightly patted him on the shoulder and let him go on his own. The sailors sent by the dignified captain to be Dick's guards were beaten like straw men, and the wharf and train became battlefields, without any interference. Unless this world is only for them to fight! "If you overdo it, it's not a play!" Someone in the audience was saying this.

Let's put these aside for now, and follow the producers to watch them fight. Frankly speaking, the fighting scenes in the film are not handled very well. It's always a matter of bumping around like bulls, and the tricks of falling from high places and the sea, climbing, and jumping off cars have lost their so-called thrilling fun due to the overuse of the old-fashioned tricks. What's more, the yellow car escaping, the black car chasing, the white steamboat escaping, and the black steamboat following, as shown on the screen, are lengthy and repetitive, making people feel a little bored?

The director's poor skills are not limited to this. For example, in the whole film, there are seven or eight places where the bad lawyer and his subordinates communicate by wire and wireless telephones, and the scenes of connecting and disconnecting the calls in these seven or eight places are exactly the same as the original. After Dick escapes from danger, in the emergency and turbulent scenes, there is always such a stagnant and slow conversation like Miss Dorothy or others. And in the conversation between two or three people, when writing about the other side's progress at the same time, no matter how much is written, when returning to the original scene, everything remains the same.

If there is anything good to say, it is the costume drama inserted in Dick's dream when his ancestors buried the treasures. The short scenes and the steady performance add a lot of color to the whole film.

This is the first episode, and we hope there will be a good show in the next episode.

Casual Talk on "The Secret of the Chateau" 225

— Guo Cheng

"The Secret of the Chateau". As the name suggests, we can imagine what a mysterious film it is.

In the castle, there is an old bell suspended in a tower. No one has ever rung it, and no one ever goes to this bell tower, but there are rumors that the bell will ring on its own, and on the night it rings, an unfortunate death will befall someone in the castle. Just imagine, what a strange tale this is?

With such a strange tale, someone took advantage of this opportunity to carry out his scheme. One day, the bell suddenly rang on its own, and the people in the castle were terrified. Sure enough, someone died that night, and a very valuable ancient book hidden in the castle also disappeared. Then, while the detectives were investigating this strange case, the bell rang again, and someone died again... How terrifying! But unfortunately, the cunning assassin carelessly revealed his identity, and the mysterious massacre was solved in a very tense situation.

The male and female protagonists of this film are played by Clark Wiuiam and Claire Dadd, and it will premiere tomorrow at the Great Shanghai Theater.

Qing Zhong Drama Society to Perform "L'Arlésienne" 226

The Qing Zhong Drama Society is scheduled to perform the world-famous play "L'Arlésienne" at the Youth Association Auditorium on Sichuan Road on the 30th and 31st of this month, with two performances in the afternoon and evening.

Film Novel

The Hate of India's Fall (Clive of India) (14) 227

— Mao De

When Clive heard this news, he immediately returned to England with Edmund. This time when he returned, there were no cheering crowds on the shore, no welcoming personnel, and even Margaret didn't come! He quietly disembarked, went ashore, and returned to his old house in Queen's Square. That was his first residence, where his first child died... Cold and alone... Just like he is now cold and alone. Edmund sent Clive to the residence in Queen's Square and immediately ran to Wallcott to see Margaret, wanting to mediate between the couple.

But Margaret's heart was already set. She adopted an attitude of indifference. She neither hated nor forgave, as if it didn't matter to her. Edmund earnestly pleaded, "You can't just throw him aside like this. He still has to deal with his enemies in the House of Commons. He needs your help, comfort, and encouragement when he is being tried. If this matter is messed up, his family and life will be over. Now is the critical moment, how can you let him go it alone?"

Margaret said, "He is alone because he wants to be." Edmund said, "Maybe he is too proud to come and see you first." Margaret said, "Edmund, I have sacrificed so much. If he is proud, can't I be proud too? However, when you see him, please give him my regards." Edmund angrily said, "You have been married for so many years, and you are still talking about pride?" He said, bowed deeply, and left.

In the evening, the British House of Commons was already crowded with people, with no room to set foot, to listen to this sensational trial. Margaret, led by Captain Clark, was taken to a dark corridor with a window where she could hear everything in the House. She trembled all over and listened quietly as Sullivan stated that Clive's property was all illegally obtained. He advocated that his property be confiscated and that he be punished. She also heard Johnston say that all the abuses of patents in India were caused by Clive. He also pointed out that Mir Jafar's gift was a bribe. She also heard Bogoraine describe in a funny tone the shape of him signing the treaty in the name of Admiral Watson, and said that a despicable person who forged a signature would never refuse a bribe.

All the attacking speeches were over, and the applause gradually subsided. Robert Clive stood up to speak. Margaret listened even more breathlessly. Clive spoke in a calm voice, "Mr. Chairman, all the words attacking me have been said. I cannot answer each and every one of them. If someone is doing things in society, you can distort all his actions to attack him. But I have one sentence, that is, everything I have done is to do my best for India, for my country..."

His voice became even louder, "In today's vote, you can take away everything from me, property, titles, and reputation... Just as India has taken away everything I love..." Margaret, in the dark corridor, couldn't help but take out a handkerchief to wipe her tears... "India has taken away everything I love..." She thought to herself, with her heart and mouth in agreement. Has she been too harsh? Isn't his leaving her for his duties? For the country? How can it be said that he doesn't love India? She couldn't help but feel remorse.

Movie Ramblings 228

— Luo Ping

Janet Gaynor will star in "The Farmer Takes a Wife".

Dante's "Inferno" has begun filming by Fox, directed by Havvy Lacbman, starring Spencer Tracy and Claire Trevor.

As a branch of art, film is said to have its own characteristics. It uses action to think and explain, and the efforts of the camera and the composition of montage are enough to make it exist as itself. But in essence, it, like other branches of art and even ideology, is a reflection of objective reality.

Since film art is essentially a reflection of objective reality, its content naturally flows from this fertile ground of reality. A certain content induces a certain form. Every picture has passed through the writer's mind. Therefore, the value of a work lies not in one aspect of its content or form, nor in the multiplication or accumulation of the two, but in the unity of everything in the two.
